The remedies are applied once with the cautery through large aid, and likewise the disease that comes from the putrefaction of blood and melancholy. If you see it being cauterized, take care that this disease is at its beginning, and if it's cured according to what we have said in the division, and doesn't spread or remain, then when you doubt whether the corruption might spread throughout the diseased area, then do this: for five times cauterization on the head: one time towards the base of the skull towards the start of hair, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two times on the two horns, and one behind on the neck; and let your hand be such that the cautery reaches up to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors might escape; and cauterize gently below according to what is done above.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixture is everywhere scattered; and it becomes apparent that you must cauterize with these cauteries we have mentioned on the head, and one cauterization under the nose, and two cauterizations on the spine from the neck to the chest, and six on the spine from the back of the neck down, and one large one on the nape of the neck and another in front of it, and two on each shoulder blade; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the legs, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and around the creases of the hands; and be careful not to burn any nerves that are behind the heel bone. And do not once make a cauterization on the bone near the ankle, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more often I use the cautery, the more assistance it provides and the benefits are noticeable; and know that patients do not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people would, because their bodies have already become thoroughly corrupted. And you should make the cauteries large and small according to the limbs and joints, following what you will find in instructions about instrument procedures. After healing, rub with flour several times along with honey and other treatments until it has fully healed.
de enfleure	of inflamed
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When inflammation occurs in any limb and is treated with medicines and oils and bandages, and it does not heal, then you should perform cauteries on the limb according to its size; and make sure that a small part of each cautery enters into the tissue of the diseased area. Then treat with ointments until fully healed. And every time a cautery is performed at the hand, foot, and back, where the nerve ends and makes the limb immobile, and thus it will be removed; and always do not interfere unless you are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	From galls
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the illness named "albaras" becomes old, and conventional medicine is ineffective, then apply a small cautery burn according to the amount of the plant in question. Do this until the gallbladder is removed and its color changed. After that, wash with flour and lentils mixed with rose oil and plantain leaves, along with blood from colostrum and chicken sand, each using one part of their quantity. Mix everything together, then wrap it with a cloth, and leave it on the affected area until fully healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for a pustule by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a pustule begins to develop, and you notice it, stop its spread by applying a cautery burn that resembles a circle around the entire circumference of the pustule. And often they say that one should also apply a cauterization in the middle of the pustule; and I personally do not think this is good because I fear it might lead to ulceration and corruption, which has already happened several times for me; more straightforward would be to apply the cautery around, with a circular tool as we have described earlier among different types of cauterization tools.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When some have a disease which is called "adubelati", and it delays death or due to its excess causing harm, or due to the old age of the sick person when they are too old (meaning very old), and they have little blood, or due to the tension; and you see it hasten towards death: then cauterize around a bit of small cauterizations by pricking; afterwards leave them like that. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it being pierced through the entire cauterization, then heat the cauterizing instrument as described here:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauterizations have pierced through its entire depth, and ensure that these cauterizations are such that the patient feels a sense of relief to such an extent that the process of decay is alleviated. After treating until it becomes completely sound.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure using fire through a iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another way to treat disease, which is called 'corrodens', it is nothing more than a bodily malaise that affects members in the same way that fire burns dry sticks. If you see this illness on someone who can tolerate a cautery treatment together with heat, then make iron cauteries small and large, according to what suits the place where the illness is; after cauterizing from all sides until you burn out all corruption, and leave nothing behind, making sure that every corrupted part is removed. And then let it be for three days, and apply iron filings with oil over the cauterized parts as long as the burnt areas heal, and all the corruption. After this, the treatment of ointments causing flesh to grow. And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not emerge, it is good; and if this does not happen, start again on the cauterization where there remains corruption from the members. And this malaise is often cured with medicine in place of heat-cautery; but still, heat cautery helps much more, I have already spoken about the treatment of fever in division: take it whenever you need to.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of ulcers that come on bones
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once in a while, a disease arises from within the foot that is named "clos" according to our understanding, and it's a large hard thing that pokes the foot. The cauteries for this disease are done through two methods. That being said, fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery involves heating up one metal cautery like a goose feather tip and making sure it's made of well-forged iron in such size that it can touch every part of the nail, ensuring there are fine margins; after that you heat the stick all along its length until it reaches the very tip; then let the process continue for about three days as pus starts to form; next create a poultice of ground wild garlic mixed with oil and leave this poultice on overnight; then the nail will be removed from its roots. Afterwards, cure the wound by spreading an ointment that causes inflammation until it heals fully.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are turned inside the body, and this happens many times in feet and hands as well, it's necessary that you apply hot water cautery; and do it like this: take a reed or iron rod, or a goose feather tip, place them over the nail bed and around it, meaning on warts; then place the stick so that its heat penetrates fully into all parts of it, then put some hot water on it, hold your hand well while you turn it, making sure the edge of the stick reaches down to the nail roots, thus finding the deep path of the hot water until it reaches the root; and let the patient endure for a short time the burning from the hot water for an hour; then leave them as they are, and they will be completely uprooted. Repeat this several times until you've removed all those that have been in the body, then cure the sores that generate pus afterwards.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment involves shaking it off.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shakes from cold or nerves, or has a fever that lasts four days or another condition, it is necessary to apply four or four cauterizations on the spine of their back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one on the chest at the olive-shaped cautery; if this does not stop the shaking, then hasten the recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	The pus-filled lesions
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Any time you notice a boil or pus-filled pustules that have come from large decaying matter, if it's necessary at the beginning when they appear to cauterize each tip of the pustule: a fine fire stick cautery where the point touches the flame, or a long root of aristolochia, or an oval-shaped cautery. And never let them be cauterized right from the start when they first appear, following this method; instead they'll stop growing forward, but their excess will be resolved and they become healed. But it should be done after blood has been evacuated.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times great amounts of blood have flowed from the artery that has been cut at the wound when it comes to the one going beyond, or incision of an abscess, or the cautery on the limb, and similar things; and it is very troublesome a matter to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to none of them, should you quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press very much until the pain subsides under your finger, and no more drops flow; then apply several small and large olive oil cauteries as long as they are all red. Then take .i., or large or small depending on the wound and to the place where the artery is located, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery there until the pain stops completely.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you remove your finger from the vein, and once the cauteries are extinguished, take quickly another one of the cauterizing tools that are at the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop performing this one after another until the skin is completely incised; and beware that you do not burn the nerve underneath it, nor let any other harm come upon the patient; and know that when hair falls from the artery, one cannot properly incise it even if the artery is large, unless done through one of the four methods we have mentioned: by cautery, or extraction when it hasn't been treated yet, or by strong stringing where a ligature is placed, or with medicines applied which have the power to incision blood; and it should be bound and held in place subsequently.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer the tying or binding with cloths tightly or by putting heat-bearing things thereon, or other similar actions, if it doesn't prove effective.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no means or medicine at hand, then they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we said, and stretch it well until the skin is incised over the wound and over the vein; and do not move the hand but moisten it with cold water often that remains very cold until the skin is frozen and swollen and incised; and perform ligatures in advance for those requiring cautery and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of treatments for amputations
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have spoken in the first chapter about all diseases where it is necessary to use fire cautery or hot medicine. We discussed their uses, causes, instruments and forms of cautery; and concluded that chapter with applying them up to the foot, and I will proceed through this chapter using the same path since it seems easier to find what one wants here.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And when I begin this, it is important for you to understand that in this chapter there is more risk and fear than in the first section about using cautery, and for this reason, greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and treating wounds, and extracting arrows, and making cuts into stones, and similar matters; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I advise you not to embark in foolish endeavors. For many ways of people come into treatments. Some come from those who are deeply affected by their illness that they die slightly due to the panic they find at their sickness, and because of the severity of their disease; and from these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And among these there are those who understand and say: "Wait, I'm aware." And the disease is deceitful. It's not advisable to agree with those who come to you in this manner, but rather place more restraint on your honor than on your greediness, do not act impulsively but wisely for those whom you are certain of, and have knowledge about; and use prediction and suggestion in treatments for your patients where health is transformed. This will help you gain good reputation, glory, and long-lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, our lords give you good understanding and justice, and if you wish to aspire from the holy inspiration of their hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have instructed this chapter according to its chapters, following what is before it in the section on cauteries, which I have outlined from the head down to the feet because you will find them more easily than those you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	From the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes very often to children at birth, and when the mother presses too hard on the head of the child; and it happens in no other case for reasons unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone other than children, and among all those I've seen, their deaths came quickly; for this reason, it seems to me that I should abandon the treatment of cases like these with partial cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose shoulder joints were filled with water, and his head grew each day to the point where he could not bear it anymore; and feared so much from moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled around the bone above the siphon, between the heart and the bone; and the veins are arranged in such a way when moisture is between the heart and the bone, and abscesses are small, that you make an opening under the head a large crack; and so long as the moisture flows; and see this shape of the spathile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, make two openings in a manner like a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is within the bone, and the signs you see show that the edges of the head have opened from every part, and water spurts out when you press it inward with your hand, and this does not stop: then you should make three openings in the middle of the head like this:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, remove all moisture. After holding the cuts open with strips and powders, then apply wine and oil, and leave like that until the fifth day; then reset it, treat the wound through dressing and ointments, and let the head be held equally, thereafter allow the patient to eat dry meat from a small amount of moist for as long as the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the opening of the abscess is large, and assemble with water; because it does not always appear in front; nor always behind; nor always on the right side; nor always on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then where the abscess opens, and fill with water, and make a cut according to what you can do; and watch that you do not cut the artery; and look for a flow of blood, so that the patient dies due to the loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of cautery by fire, command to the unwell that they let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there occurs a disease which is called "catarrh" to the eyes or at the bottom (of the body), and the disease is old, and the treatment with medicine doesn't help, then the last resort of treatment could be cautery using what one would cauterize their two major arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	So then, if you cover your eyes, the patient should let their head be placed after their neck; afterwards rub a rough cloth on it until the arteries are visible, and then pull out the diseased part of the body by all means with one cloth. Then look where the veins lie, and see how far apart the eyes are from each other, and when they're properly repositioned; then mark the eyes with a cross, and cauterize both of them with an acutely heated piece of metal for about half an hour until the skin turns black up to the bone, and this should be done around the width of their head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, stop the bleeding from beneath the artery and above the cut, by making a cut also like one inch through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, let the blood flow out continuously from up top.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open upon touching, it is necessary that you measure the length of the space to about three inches, then pierce until you reach the bone; and what needs to be removed from the blood is about seven parts per centum, and by chance a little more or less depending on what the patient can endure, and the replenishment of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone slightly yellowish, and if the incision above our abscess does not show, then press down the wound and bandage it, and apply ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	Of the removal
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old age comes, and acute cough, because of the moisture from tears and heat in the temples and lower back that is beyond endurance and similar things. Medicine is treated with ways of medicinal cures and all this does not help him, so we extract the arteries in the temples and cauterize them, as we have reported.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is such that one feels beneath their temple hair, and hears about the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well by its pulsation, and is only responsive in some who are too cold; and if it responds, then strain his neck with some cloth strips, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and heat him up with hot water until the artery becomes clearly evident. Then take the spatula as shown below:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it up high with forceps, and remove many threads that are from each part; and if the artery is fine, if you twist it at the tip of the nail, then cut across that part according to the number of two bones. For if she isn't cut, neither will all be torn completely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And drain the blood from the .vj. c, until the third day; and if the artery is large, then it should be tied in two loops of a strong double thread of silk, so that infection does not occur before the healing of the wound, nor repeatedly bleed; then cut off the excess between the two threads at that moment, and then, if you see, then apply the cautery gently until the bone with the bones being cut; and this is the surgical procedure, should the patient not have fever and be of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery helps to finish off infections: for this reason it is a greater help against infections.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	When it comes to extracting arteries, one must fill the area with old cotton and place well-made tent cloths over it; when you sever them, apply dry medicinal substances that promote tissue growth, as well as tent cloths until it heals. And if you don't have a proper clamp for the artery, act just as you would during extraction, hurry to use a cautery tool, or utilize the area with vitriol and grip your hand tightly so that the clot stays in place; and if you lack this present tool, apply ice on the clot until it freezes, then immerse the affected area in cold water until the clot no longer moves, ensuring proper restraint. The one who is faster and lighter during artery extraction should cauterize the blood vessel from that cautery trenching for half an inch, but make sure the trenching is well spaced to retain heat for a longer duration.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they retain less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be .i. inch of space between the two knives, and when you have heated them to touch both ends, place the hot iron until it reaches the bone, then cauterize the vessel in two places; and keep them spaced apart for these shoulder joints because there is no soldering on this cautery tool throughout; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears of the eyes are descending through the veins that are above the testicle of the head of the arm, and it does not benefit from any treatment with medicine that one might do, and you see the face of the patient turning red, and feel or see a pulsation as if of a heartbeat; and where they are tender and moist so that the hairs on paper fall off, and the papers become heated, and burned by the heat of the tears, it is necessary to have this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called the old one "the treatment for contusion", and you should do this: bring the hair to the front of the patient who has this disease, then make three cuts on the front, evenly according to the length of the forehead; let one of these cuts extend as if two-thirds down the entire forehead from above, until it reaches the bottom edge, and the other ones are made at both sides of the ribs under the papers. And be careful not to cut any arteries that are under the ribs; keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and each wound should have three doings across them;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have ready a piece of sponge and some cloths to wipe off the blood, then ignite the ague brazier from two parts of it where this is formed:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the cut that is near the temple up to the second cut; and burn all the flesh that is between the two gaps evenly until it sticks to the bone, then make another cut from the middle cut up to the other gap, and then extract this ague brazier.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you ignite in the first gap the tool called 'cultellaire', and it is very sharp on one side, but blunt on the other, it has this shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. And place the cutting side of the tool towards the soft flesh at the bone, and the blunt edge towards the bone, and ignite until it reaches to the middle cut. And remove all the vessels that descend from the head to the veins up to where the incision is continuous up to the one that opens in the bone, and then make another cut halfway into the middle cut up to the other gap; and then extract the blood evenly, and express the head for the blood taken; then place a cloth of old cotton in each gap, and put wet cloths with wine and oil and garlic, and ensure no pus enters; and on the third day release the stitches, and apply large bandages soaked in vinegar, then perform the ointment cure with basil oil and olive oil, and other treatments for wounds until it heals.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When there is an acute catarrh accustomed, and you see the eyes swollen and small, and weakening of sight, and burnt paper; and hair falls out, and one feels a feverish chill, and the patient sneezes. Therefore, know from these events that those substances and this mucus come only from many veins, and the remedy used, if it is such.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you should command the patient to lie down on their back, then make a large incision through the forehead and another wide. Start by making an incision from the left temple to the right temple along the hairline; cut until you reach the bone. Keep your hand away from the temples' nerves which move during eating. When the bone is exposed, drain all blood using a sponge, then clean inside the two incisions with old cotton and linen cloths. Apply wrung cloths soaked in wine and oil above, taking care not to remove any scabs. Once it's removed, you should rub the bone until the new flesh begins to grow, then treat it with exfoliating substances that promote growth.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of the flower of wheat and four parts of colofoin, make them into a paste; and apply it to these wounds to stimulate flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding ear piercing.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that is inserted into the ears is one of the four things: or seeds, or beast, or mine stones or similar things such as iron; or seeds, such as beans, peas; or flowing matter such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When he inserts a piece of metal or another kind of thing into the ear that doesn't fit or grow in the ear, place the ear under the sun. If you can see the metal piece, then apply a drop of violet oil or saffron oil; and after this, treat with extraction; make him sneeze with conditi, and stuff his nostrils when the sneezing comes, put pieces of cloth or wool into the ear; and place the ear above. Many times this cure works; and if it doesn't work, then apply extraction using fine needles, which is described here:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it leaps like needles, that's good; if not, prepare for the extraction using a small, sharp instrument with slight curvature; and if it doesn't leap through these, make an araneus needle and pinch the tip of the needle or part of the ear well, then soak whatever is inside the wax of the needle so that the wick cannot enter with the needle; then press the wax firmly for use because many times it comes in like we said; and if it doesn't come in this manner, take glue from it and pinch its ends, and place in some an instrument suitable for such work, and put a bit of cotton inside; then press the glue onto the stone or anything else, and pull.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't leap through all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear so an abscess bulges out and spasms; and the way of cutting is such that you first sharpen the edge of the patient's auricular lobe, and extract blood according to its size, then let the lobe lie between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the base of the ear near the fat or what hangs down; and make the cut as round as a moon until you reach the stone, then break the bone according to your strength, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and treat until it is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it's grains that are inside and it swells, prepare for extraction; and if it cannot come out, prepare this small spatula tool according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And prepare for the incision of that grain. But do not perform this when you think that the grains are moist due to the moisture in the ear, until you have done many pieces; then extract with fine pincers and a suction pump, as we have said, so that the extractions happen smoothly.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In water then, where the patient sneezes in their ear, make sure they use a small amount of condiments first and fully expand the ear with old cotton. And be lying right next to that ear where the water is located. If it jumps out through this, that's good. If not, take several pieces according to the length of your fingers and softly, heat them slightly on fire; then place one or two of these heated pieces into their ear, and blow out with your other foot from another part, and do the same thing with another piece on the piece where the water is in the ear. And continue doing this from piece to piece until all the water comes out completely, and thus it jumps out completely; and if you see, take one small stick, place one of these ends into their ear, and apply fire to the other end as long as the more tender part burns; then redo with others sticks until all the water is out, just like what we've said about stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of small creatures like a flea and such, treat them as we have said in division. Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. de l’estoupement des oreilles	From ear piercing
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any perforation in the ears; and this same thing happens at home through ear piercing wounds, or of a fetus being born inside the ear, and these piercings happen once within the ear, if one cannot see them; and never does it have .i. hole for the perforation to be seen, and one sees it very well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes within the ear, if one cannot see it, is due to gunk being sanitized in various positions, and you must understand that putting the ear by the fire helps; look inside: if you can see the obvious inflammation, if the work has fully created this pus-like substance described here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be cut and dug out from front to back all evenly, so that it does not burn the ear; if the inflammation is due to pus or part of the ear, hold your sharp tools gently until that pus-filled part is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. And if the excrescence is deep in the ear, take one sharp and light rasor, then heat a small part of it on fire. Place this near the ear. If you feel the excrescence that causes pain in the ear when touched lightly by the skin, pierce it slightly, making sure not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place a wick inside the ear according to its width, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Continue this action every day until the wound is healed, or take a wick and moisten it with rose water, and apply powdered vitriol. And if you see swelling in the ear, then remove the wick and replace it with another dampened one made from rose oil and beeswax, until the swelling disappears; then continue treating it until it is healthy again.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse a cloth and dip it in cold water, then place it on the ear, and apply other treatments that stop bleeding which are known from distillation processes.
de la char des papieres	From the page's contents
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet. And if you don't remove them, cauterize them with a fine cone cautery and the cauterizer after the incision will be beneficial; they should repair themselves many times over, as nothing remains from their roots. de la gresle	Of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times in the papers do you find some things that seem hard and dense by their form and hardness, for this is called "granuloma" disease, and it's a collection of thick moisture on top and underneath the paper; the procedures are as follows: take care if the granuloma moves from one side to another, and it's a simple matter to know about this; then make cuts broadly, after that lightly cauterize each part, then pinch the granuloma and extract. If you cannot extract without piercing some of the paper, or causing any harm to the patient; if the tear is large, and there's an opening, cure until it heals completely; and if it's small, don't apply too much force, for ointments restore and renew flesh quickly.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granuloma is descending within the ear towards the upper part, invert the paper and place the granuloma under the scissors, then extract and press from both sides; and if the paper is pulled away by the cut, it causes no harm; and when the granuloma has been extracted, remove the salty water, cure the wound until the flesh is renewed, so that the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the granulomas
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Exinach is a kind of fat that can be found in the sheets of paper above, and this happens more with children than adults, and it causes great distress to their eyes. It comes to them at dawn and they cannot look at sunlight because tears rush into their eyes; therefore, they sleep on their sides always, and lie down on their papers so that they are moist under their eyelids, which then gets filled with exinach and changes the appearance of both their eyes and outer area from it. And when you press your hand onto this area and feel the exinach between your fingers.

And the way of doing this surgery is that the patient places their head on your healthy area. From this slit, the exinach comes out in various positions according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then remove it all in one piece of cloth between your fingers at the front, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed; make sure not to stick in the slit, that you don't get inside the moist area up to the eye, that you don't hurt it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not open at the beginning of the wound, so enlarge a little bit gently the wound until it opens; then stretch as we have said, then moisten with cloths and water, and place on the limb, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are people who grind flour and place it to corrupt the moisture that has remained. Then treat him until he is sound. And if an abscess appears on the limb, then the treatment with healing plasters continues until he is sound.
des poilz des papieres	The phrase "des poilz des papieres" translates directly to "the hairs of papers". This might refer to paper fibers or could be metaphorical depending on context. Without more information, this is the literal translation.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hair grows in different places than naturally does and it becomes grey, these affect the eyes causing diseases like constant watering from them and paper-like swelling of the eyelids and puffy eyes, due to being a cause of eye damage; then treatment should be conducted according to four methods: or by fire cautery as an ensemble, or through blood-letting medicine as described in the chapter about cautery, and this is done either through incision and stitches or with bandages, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the eye socket in its natural position, then turn the paper of the eye onto your left hand; if it flips over correctly, that's good; if not, sew through one thread from point .i. on top; and do this either beyond the edge of the paper or where hair grows underneath these hairs, pull through a single thread all across the paper and then fold it back with a razor; then cut out part beneath the paper, beneath these hairs, extending to the corner up to the small one; then remove a thread, place a tiny cotton tent and linen on the paper, then draw an emblem onto the paper as round as a bay leaf, but ensure that the emblem matches the height you see when lifting the folded paper.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there's need for a large amount of paper according to how the paper has been softened; then stitch up the entire area above the two lines you've marked, starting from the corner to the small one; and make sure that you have one of the cuts next to the natural hairs in their growth stage as big as a root, then place the needle in one of the corners of this circle, then burn all around it; then stitch together both lips with a thread using two fine wool threads everywhere, and cleanse out any blood, then let air dry the excess threads on both eyebrows for some things stick there if done properly; and if you don't see that happening, pay no mind to it, then leave the stitches alone until days .iij. or .iiij.; then treat the wound without stitching with desiccating and constraining substances because the paper heals from the immediate contact of the wound and its assembly process, but the stitches become moist (as they used to say), and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if you have another way: and then you mark the paper with a figure that is as like the leaf of myrtle, just as we recounted it, in one inch squares according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take what stands above the smaller forces evenly according to the shape which is here:

et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz. li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The surgical operations are like this: you take a fine needle and tie it with two strands of silk thread which is fine and strong. Then join the ends together finely, making sure they're long enough for one palm to measure between them. Next, place another strand of the fine silk thread across in your hand, tying its ends around the needle's shaft; then insert this end into the injured person's wound until it pierces through natural hair thickness and then quickly moves back out beyond the hairline on paper. When you have pulled all hairs to that point, remove your hand letting them come out completely from the paper with their original hair length.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the needle is treated and no hair comes out with it, you should pull the needle from all the silk thread that was ordered in your hand, until the needle reaches its end point which is just beyond where it pierced the skin. Then you check to see this visually through the eye; then remove the needle and the thread, and rest the eye for two days or three days, until the hair grows back to its original place and a new flesh begins to form. And if the hairs are small, accompany them with one long hair from a living animal, letting it grow along with the one you left or trim it, once it's grown out fully before cutting.
de la porriture de l’oil	Regarding eye infections
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this illness, called 'aleacrati' or rot in the eye, comes about, there are two ways it can happen: one naturally and the other unnaturally. Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the matter that comes to the eye

This disease which truly is called 'axacrati', and is natural and accidental. dou soudement de la papiere	right along the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez. de l’ungle de l’oil	From the edge of the eye

Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	None of these are born or are nears, they consist of various joined flesh parts; and among them some seem like scorpions with beaks of birds. And if there is such a case where the flesh is filled with dark color, and if it has good-colored flesh. Therefore, for this kind of flesh which is good-colored and not filled, you should have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; work on their nostrils, pour vinegar onto those parts of flesh, and push them out; then hold what you can bear at the delicate sharp edge on one side until you know that that piece of flesh is entirely bone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is no thing that we cannot cope with, if the opening is done with all one instrument delicately and lightly, ensuring nothing remains; and if it does not ascend or have pus at its bottom, then you should cleanse it accordingly. And if there are abscesses, cut them out straight away; and for bad abscesses, act quickly and use a cautery until the pus is drained out completely and all the sinews have been treated. Then drain or bleed freely or with water or wine afterwards.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And if the nose operation is necessary, and moisture reaches up to the palate, know that it has infected; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there's new flesh inside the bone above, which doesn't come down to cut: thus you must insert one piece of linen thread slightly thick into his mouth and tie it with your hand, making sure each knot is spaced about an inch or less. And put the patient's nose to this linen rope through their nostril, pulling gently until it comes out through the nostril within the mouth; and do this many times for children in schools, and it's a simple task for those who wish to perform it; then hold the head that comes out of the nostril with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, knowing them one after another as you guide them with our hands. Do this until you know that the knot has rotten all the flesh, then remove the thread, clean the blood, oil the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose exactly as before; do this for three days or more, until the medicine rots whatever is left of the flesh; and after that place a cumin stick for several days until it heals, and if there's need for dried medicines, use them; and this is the form of instrument to purify the head, in which one distills oils and medicines with the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And use it made of silver or tin, resembling an open lamp, like a rod, and guide it in the same way; and if you see fit, make it into a closed rod, and fill the instrument to purify the head; and keep one hand on the head when heating the oil or any other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh around the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease is born around the nose at the root of the nose, which is called "telul", it grows and becomes large until you can see it; and because this must be handled in the beginning, and the bone should be prepared completely, then place it under your control with the cautery or the burning medicine; and if you delay preparing it until it's large, beware if it feels hard, if it changes color, if there is a poor sense: don't touch it with iron for it is an infected abscess, because when you remove it once, it brings great harm to the patient; and if the abscess was due to heat exposure, not from changing color, and you see that all can be removed, then empty the patient and perform surgery with fear, and treat the area with desiccating and restricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and stitched
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when the joints of this chapter come into solution, it benefits little, in some people. So you must ensure this does not happen to any, if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then adjust the two lips towards one stitch, afterwards treat until they are healed; and should the lips be completely dried from one side and the other, it is necessary that you sear all parts of their skin until they heal, then join the two lips together by one stitch, and press them, dusting with dragon's blood powder and incense. And place the powders on a piece of plaster or another bonding plaster, let this sit until it discharges itself, then treat with ointment until they are healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is such that you join the paste: or by needles, as we have said in the stitch for the abdomen; or with thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	from abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the hands of someone within the abscess, there are stones like grains sometimes, smaller and larger; therefore it must be that you remove the lips, cut into each pit, take them with forceps and extract in each part; then after the vitriol incision, apply pressure to the wound until bleeding stops; and then clean the wound from dry things until it is clean.
de la char des gencives	from the flesh of the gums
