Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, a hard flesh forms on the gums, which the old called "albulus"; it must be held with forceps and cut to its root, allowing for bleeding or blood flow. Then place under the heat of vitriol broiet powder, or other powders that restrict and dry out; and if this flesh returns after cutting, and does so many times, then cut it a second time and cauterize it: if it doesn't return after being cauterized; these are the forms used for cutting.
des sordens	Of cauteries with fire command the sick person to let the hairs grow long and evenly; if they pierce at their root, hold the eyes firmly so they don't move until they fully grow.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Many times teeth assemblies are gathered at the main part of the teeth, between the mouth and gums; you'll find ugly and harsh layers here. And many times blackened and citrine teeth along with worms exist until the infection reaches the gum line, and the teeth become stinky too. Therefore, it's necessary to place the sick person under your hands, have their head on a holy surface, and hold out any teeth or layers that are visible till nothing remains; then you should take care of blackness and greenness, yellowing, and other colorations until they disappear. And if one removes what is at first sight obvious, it's good; otherwise, start again after the second day and the third, until you have everything removed. And remember that teeth require different types of instruments to be extracted depending on how the work is done, as the tool used for extraction differs from those placed between teeth; these forms along with others should be ready with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It's necessary that when you treat the tooth for its pain, you delay the extraction as much as possible because one should not do this in haste. As it is a very delicate matter, there should be no reason to rush during the process.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore when the patient is forced to extract teeth, you must be certain about which tooth is causing trouble. Often during pain, the patient fears it might be a holy tooth, and so they want to remove a good tooth; yet until the bad tooth is removed, some of the pain remains, as we have already desired for these soldiers; and when you are well certain about which tooth is causing trouble, then you should scorch around that tooth up to one spatium very strongly in order to protect the gum from all sides. Then move your hands or with your fine forceps at first try and try, until it is properly extracted, then firmly secure those forceps; and have the shoulder of the patient under holy water between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it doesn't jump out, take none of these instruments and push it in from every part lightly, then move it as you did first. And if the tooth is pierced and fractured, then it's necessary to fill it with cloths where they were lost; and if you extract it slightly with your fine forceps, so that it doesn't break while being extracted; and it must be very carefully opened around the gum in order to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And you must carefully ensure that you do not break it and leave part of the tooth behind, which will cause greater pain due to the malice of the root than at first. And be careful not to act like ignorant soldiers who, through their haste and rashness, break everything once and do not follow our advice; but instead they bring about the disease by cutting into the roots that remain or breaking the tooth itself, as we have often advised. When the tooth has been removed, wash off your hand with wine or vinegar and water; and if bleeding occurs (which often happens), then fill your hand with vitriol paste; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments you first use should have long points and thick handles, ensuring they don't double when you pull the tooth; these are their forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And may have large limbs that do not bend while being used, and be made of strong iron well-crafted, with teeth for gripping.
de la racine des dens	from the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains during extraction, it is necessary to place wet cotton in the mouth with butter for one or two days until the gums are softened. Then remove the forceps which are called 'algefri', making the shoulder appear as a surgeon's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, this is their form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out completely with these pliers, it is necessary that you uncover the entire flesh up to the root, and place the instrument known as "althali," which means palmache, as it is formed thus:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be hollow and thick so that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps out through this, that's good; if not, use all the tools you have, as their shapes follow after these descriptions:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if help is taken from this tool which has two points, as it is formed thus:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front according to the size of teeth, and this tool which seems like large pliers, as it is formed thus:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let there be this instrument so it may not break, and know that few of the instruments of dentistry are; also other instruments which are not counted among them. And as such, skilled masters find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their works and diseases reveal to them, for there are some illnesses for which old teachers did not teach any instrument due to the variety within them and if any part breaks from the tooth or of another bone, or it rots, they look for the instruments that suit them, which I have mentioned, and help through gestures, as is this form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well designed to hold the bone, so that it doesn't escape, but can be held and removed; and then restore him with medicines suitable for this situation. If there is decay in the bone, and if it's small, when using this instrument take care of all these aspects:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth do not appear naturally and their form is ugly, especially in young girls where teeth are born after the first ones and cannot be pulled or filed: in such cases you must know that it's due to the teeth being born in a crooked position. Therefore, extraction is necessary; and if they are alongside another tooth, take this tool described here with this shape, similar to one small hook each, made of sharp iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the tooth is ground slowly with my hands day by day due to the hardness of its root, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be filed, then I file it in a single piece like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it's also like the file used for making needles; and I grind the tooth slowly with my hands day by day gently, so that it doesn't move until it chips; then in the end level off everything completely with no sharp edges left, and if its edge is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then you must grind down the roughness until it's even, so as not to hurt the tongue or ruin speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth rots
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth are dislodged due to blow or impact, and if the patient cannot press on them as they chew without vomiting, indicating a problem; you must have cured it with medicines that restrict this, but it doesn't work. In such cases, it is necessary to restrain them using gold thread; for silver threads turn green and decay over time, whereas gold does not change in color or degrade ever. The size of the thread should be moderate – neither too thick nor too thin – according to the space between the teeth. If you see that the teeth have aligned correctly again after insertion, take a thread and a needle twice as wide as one healthy tooth slot in between two healthy teeth slots. When there are more than one dislodged tooth, place it so that its tip reaches to the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue covering up until you reach where you had covered before. Gently pull your hand while applying pressure, ensuring no movement of the dislodged teeth. Securely tie it at the root of the tooth so they cannot escape. Then cut the threads with tweezers and join them together again, placing them between the healthy teeth slots, making sure not to irritate the tongue; then leave it there as tight as possible without causing discomfort or pain. If they slip away or the threads break, secure them with another thread; if it stays in place and serves its purpose throughout its usage period, this is the proper alignment of your teeth and their correct joining of two healthy tooth slots and two dislodged tooth slots as you can observe:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the teeth are set back in their place, they should be reinserted gradually, as we have mentioned; do not interfere with anything that is not cautious and can tolerate it, and never shape them like an osseous tooth of a calf. Place them in the spot where the defect exists, and secure them as we have said, and let them stay and serve for as long as they can.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	covering the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	No time is spent discussing ailments that come from the tongue or nature itself, which are born this way; or by accident due to wound healing. And the procedures involve working on the mouth with disease, having your head in a healthy position, and lifting the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament from the large area, until the tongue is removed from its place, and if there is hardness or swelling, particularly due to sudden wound healing, you should pull the hook and cut that ligament; and ensure that the incision isn't made too deep as it could reach the artery; and when finished, lift the head from a pinkish or reddish water, then apply ice underneath the tongue; and each night cleanse your tongue to prevent sogginess. And if bleeding occurs again, place sulfur powder inside the wound; and if there is no relief, cauterize with the slow burning cautery, which works well for this situation; then proceed with other treatments until healed
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you notice anything that appears to be bloodied, black or hard, and your patient doesn't feel it, don't touch it as it could be gangrene; and should it start to turn into pus, and there is moisture, then use a hook to drain it and make a small incision from both sides, removing it from top and bottom; and if the pus remains in your body operation, place sulfur powder until it's healed, then continue with your operations as long as you have strength. Then lift the head with cool water and salt, and proceed with other treatments until complete healing occurs.
des apostemes de la gorge	From throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	No time comes within the throat cavities which are called 'godath', and they are properly known as the two almond-shaped ones. And when you treat them, as we have discussed in division, and if they're not sound, always take care: If these are pus-filled small bumps of little sense and a reddish color, do not touch them with iron at all. And if they're red and their root is large, don't touch them with iron either; it's because of the bleeding tendency; but leave them until they are injured, then you will remove them, or they would split by themselves. And if they're of pale color and have a subtle root, get your tool ready to cover them, but first make sure these pus-filled areas are calm and settled. Then place the patient under the sun's rays, keep their limbs in their natural state, and let the body mouth open and the servant squeeze the tongue all around with his hands on the whole instrument; it's this form; and be made of silver or finely casted metal like knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue on all this instrument? And you see pus. Take the incision and put it in an almond, then pull it up more than you can; and don't remove any thing with, then shape it with your hands as it should be, which resembles some strength; and always both parts of head are corbed, and one part another, and are very sharp, and made of iron or fine tin:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument at hand, then shape it with pliers, which should resemble the form described above:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting on one side and the other part of the name; and when you have done with one of the almonds, do the other in the same manner, and after making the cut gargle the patient with hot and cold water, or with water that is cool and mild. If bleeding occurs during this, then gargle the patient with hot water, or with cooked pieces of pomegranates, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the wound is healed; then finish the treatment when it becomes healthy again. And do not let anything else grow in the throat other than the two almonds if you proceed thusly regarding them.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, one small in size; and had almost completely sealed off all the throat, so much so that the woman could not breathe through the obstructed passage or eat or drink anything, dying after about one day or two. The abscess was so high that it had forced the insertion of two pins through both nostrils. I acted promptly then, inserting a small incision in one side and pulling out a large portion of mucus; afterwards, filled another nostril with water. Then opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards inserted a pin in these abscesses, removed some of it, only letting out a little blood; thus opened the passage to the throat of the woman, started now drinking cold water then wine, did not cease cutting that abscess over an extended period of time; and the abscess would reappear immediately, filling up with liquid as I had emptied before until it became very large; then treated her and cauterized inside the throat: thus remained without growing again; and was left in those parts, only let God do anything with her after me.
de l’uve	from the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the head of the shoulder is descending towards the elbow and it swells and grows long, this situation is called "perpendicular". And if it is swollen and round in size, then it is referred to as an "elbow". When it has been treated following our instructions from the previous division but shows no improvement, and you notice that the wound or abscess area calms down due to small movements - similar to what we have experienced - then you should first reset any dislocation.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place our head with a hair or where we apply the medicine, like the movements of a spoon, and place the instrument with all of the medicine on the elbow; let the patient remain still on his side so that saliva and fluid from his mouth can be drawn by the medicine internally, without it descending into the throat or causing distress. Then hold your hand on top of the medicine and press it onto the elbow for about half an hour until you see it absorbed and the medication's effects are calmed; if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around any tool, soak it in the medicine, stick the tool with all the cotton into a wick from above, until the cotton dries on the elbow. Repeat this often until the cautery of the medicine is perfect, then let it dry, and clean after four or five days. If you need to restart the medicine cautery procedure, do so, and after that, use a cotton plug soaked in butter inside the elbow area, cleanse everything around the medicine; rinse with cold water and gargle until fully healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision, nor than the cautery; if it's treated with fumigation according to this method, take calamus and myrrh and oregano and rue and chamomile and borage and similar herbs, and assemble all of them or any of these in one pot, and put it there, and bring it to a boil; and the pot must be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot place one tool stick according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And may be made of silver or iron, and make sure that one of the shoulder bones is in the mouth near the sore until the vapor rises up to the lungs through the nose, until the lung becomes necrotic; after this, repeat often, until the lung dries out, and remember not to do this at the beginning of the coming of pus blood, as many things occur; and don't do this tool when pus blood is receding. And if that tool isn't present, take a stick and put a bit of egg shell inside your nose, so that the mouth near the sore doesn't get too hot; for the egg shell doesn't let the vapor weigh down the mouth, and it's a good treatment together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times there's an opening in the bone or spine of a fish, with nothing else happening; so it would be suitable for you to extract what you can see and press your tongue at noonday on all the instrument, so that you can see movement happen; and that which doesn't open up inside the throat, then you should make the patient vomit as soon as possible so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it escapes through vomiting; or if the fish has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a bit of navel, or a root of lettuce, or one piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, then swallow it again; and when she comes back up to the top, if it smells good, and then proceed with extraction; and if it doesn't come out from what we have said, then take one tool of thong according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be directed towards the throat so that they can enter more lightly into the mouth, and have the head elevated up high; and guard not to touch the epiglottis, that nothing goes beyond it, nor push any bone inside; and move in such a way that the patient pushes the instrument, because if there is movement or if something becomes slippery; if she pushes the swallow, or pulls forcefully with all the instrument evenly, until she has the strength.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the substance of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No treatment has been made of the substance of the throat as I have explained in the division through medicine therapy. If this does not bring improvement, then look into the throat towards the patient's condition when you press their tongue with the instrument that I told you about. And if you see the substance, treat it with one small uncinate or fine tweezers suitable for this task. And if this doesn't help, take a wet hair and insert it into the affected area of the throat until it becomes hot after half an hour, then do this frequently. Also dye the patient's condition with water all day. Take a full glass of cold water and work their mouth, pour it in without making them swallow, and move it often with your hand; and as soon as the substance feels the water, they will vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if she does not urinate as we have said, subfumigate the patient with aloe, using the instrument mentioned in the treatment of the eyelid; do this multiple times because it will relieve without cutting. And the method for fumigation is to take one pot containing charcoal, and place its cover pierced in the middle, and at the edge of that pot is where you should put the head of the instrument. Then release your fumigation, have the patient hold the tip of the stick near their mouth, and seal the mouth so that no smoke escapes but goes up to the nostrils; and now the discharge will occur, if she does not urinate, repeat this fumigation multiple times; and make sure the patient is thirsty, eat salty foods among others, do not drink water at all; then it's necessary for her to relieve herself under this procedure.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument to treat the discharge is like having hinged curved scissors for it to enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a surgeon's hook, and it also has a roughness like that of a file, so whatever she takes, she cannot leave; and here is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	No mention of abscess formation are there according to the memory coming after this from one and another in this book, they differ in perforation and surgery; it is done in two ways where one mirrors its own appearance and concerns moisture. And the second way occurs through the veins within the body. for the abscesses at the head are different than those at the foundation, and the abscesses from lean flesh are different than those that come at joints, each has their judgement in practice.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And when it comes to abscesses, one should not pierce them until the swelling subsides according to its maturation; and for those that need piercing once they have formed, and do not subside according to their maturation, such as abscesses at joints. For when abscesses form from joints, if left intact until they are rotten internally, by chance, the ligament and nerve of the joint will rot due to this reason causing it to result in contraction within that limb. Or if the abscess is inside the main limb itself, if you delay perforation until it is rotten, it will harm the main limb; or if it's inside the foundation, piercing it should be done immediately after its rotting; and one should not pierce a forming abscess without complete maturation digestion, except for that which is in the foundation, where it might rot completely from the inside, remain buried within, and cause a fistula; and cannot heal fully over an extensive period.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It is necessary for you to know the time of abscess perforation that corresponds with maturation, and this is when the pain subsides, and the departure of fever, and reduction of pain and redness, and with the movement and hardening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; it is recommended that you have the perforation placed in the location below the abscess or at the point where it opens up, and also in line with the body length. The piercing should be made longitudinally along the body, whether the abscess is near hands or feet, joints and nerves, arteries, or any other place without a fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those that bend, according to the member in question. And when abscesses are within the fatty tissue, it should be known that you must let the punctures remain until digestion is fully accomplished, as we have said before. For if you pierce them prematurely, they will become elongated inside the body, filled with pus; and may harden the skin and the underlying flesh. And when there are no abscesses pierced through the width of the body, according to what each member requires. It is necessary that you handle small abscesses, small cuts; and in large abscesses, large cuts, and many fissures according to the size of the abscess; and if such abscesses require cauterizing with a rod, and covering them; once it has reached about the size of one hand's width, and is flattened out, then it must be handled as one would handle boils: And for those that are divided into three angles, and for those that require treatment like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses from angles; and for those that undergo a round cut, and other cuts and similar treatments.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those without a head, such as superficial abscesses, it should be that you pierce them completely. And when the abscess is large, and has grown with plenty of pus, you should pierce; but do not extract all of the pus in one go, instead take out only part of it. Then let the abscess cool until another day, then leave no treatment for now; perform this repeatedly from small to large sizes, till the pus is completely out. Similarly, if the patient has weak constitution, or women bearing children, or small infants, or elderly and decrepit individuals. For their bodies may violently react with the release of pus, causing the abscess to die without you noticing. Thus, proceed with this treatment carefully. When you have pierced your abscess, should there be a wound, observe if it's from the abscess; and see whether the wound is small; if it's a clear cut, use linen or old cotton for dressing; and if it's a large abscess and there are many cushions, then each cushion needs to be supported so they touch one another. And should you have removed a part of the skin in your abscess, having stitched inside, then fill with old cotton or linenshreds without moisture, and bind till three days; then cleanse, and apply ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs in your body part, cool water and ease should be applied along with a moist handkerchief, and place it on the wound repeatedly. And if the bleeding persists, then you should take control and treat properly, using the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is about ivor (ivory) or your limbs are very nervous, then apply wet cloths and linen soaked in wine and oil to the affected area. And if it is skin, and the wound is fatty, then applying moistened cloths with water, oil, or cold wine and oil until the third day works well, as we have said; and then release the abscess and clean it, treating properly till it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this one should be known universally in treatments of abscesses: now I have told you how one must proceed before the treatments of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of the stomach
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	When small abscesses occur in the head, they are handled similarly to how we deal with them on fabrics, like the gallbladder of a sheep. There are many similarities here. Some have fat and contain moisture just like chicken; others have a hard and stony texture under the scalpel and there's no doubt that it is an artery opposing this treatment. And in cutting, what follows is the size of your instrument, called "entromissoire", which appears as follows: something it contains. If it contains moisture, you make the incision long enough from above. And when the moisture has drained, you peel off the skin that contains that moisture without leaving anything behind; for it will return immediately if nothing is left undone. Then immerse cotton in Egyptian ointment if available; if not, use water and vinegar, apply to the wound, let sit until tomorrow; and this process goes on throughout the night. And then restart the cotton in the same manner as before, the second day, and the third, until you know clearly that it does not remain overnight; then treat the wound with ointment until it heals properly. And if the abscess contains fat for a good amount of time, cut according to this shape longitudinally; drain all its secretions, peel off from all sides, apply your entire treatment directly onto the cloth where it is located; and if the artery reacts against you, do as I told you after that. Similarly, handle pierce abscesses when they are stony, cut with the scalpel and treat accordingly as I instructed.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And when dealing with incisions on the abscesses or moist areas, they are lighter because there is less blood. And if there's no moisture in any of these abscesses or at their base, and two such abscesses that I observed at the head of an old woman; and found the abscess just like a soft stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if one had pierced none of them, one would also have treated them as well as with a stone. In other cases coming out or at their bases, it was that those which come from the heads of children and roots of ears, the opening should always be as long as possible depending on its location, for the bowels to discharge; and treat them as they should be treated.
des scrophules	regarding the pock marks
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times abscesses occur at the neck and under the armpits, as well as in the groin, and never elsewhere or on the chest. And they are round, being bound together. Each scrophula is properly within its own compartment, like a nut and an abscess at the head, as we have said; and there are many appearances of these scrophulas. Some contain moisture, and others are malign ones that do not want to obey treatment. In such cases where you see good disposition in the surgeon's hand, and it resembles the color of blood, and silent from all sides and is neither close to the throat nor near an artery or a passage, and is neither deep; then it should be that you capture it from above, and scrape each part, and if necessary make the two edges of the scrophula against the collarbone, as we have said about abscesses at the head. And treat it little by little, and be sure not to cut the nerve or vein, and do not let the moisture pool nor trench too far, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it doesn't allow you to open, place vitriol paste or any powders that clot blood in the wound, and restrain the wound; leave it until the abscess is relieved, and the wound has softened, then begins to heal. And when the blood has clotted, return to your work until you finish; then determine according to your skill whether there are no small scabs remaining, if they remove and clean them away. And if there's a large opening in the root of the ulcer, it is not suitable for cutting into that scab at its root but tie it with a thick double thread, leave it to fall off on its own without harm; then cover the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then start treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the entire ulcer, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them now, then there should be no excess left due to the size of the ulcer. It is necessary that you attend to cutting into its root, drain out fluid, and sew as we have said earlier. Those ulcers caused by excess, puncture where it appears open; do so in the same way as described before, hanging down, then apply bandages with ointment and similar things until they decay; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat it with ointment until it is healed, until it becomes healthy.
de squinance	"De squinance" translates to "on squinting" or "concerning squint". This term could be referring to medical treatments or observations related to eye disorders where one eye may be turned inward (intorsion) or outward (extorsion). The specifics would depend on the broader context of the text that this phrase is found in.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones told and spoke of the surgery to cut the throat; but I never saw anyone perform this in our land, it's written down from their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have strabismus, it is necessary that the incision of the throat known as 'the epiglottis' be made; and one should not attempt this by oneself, because all the veins and the lung are connected to those who have an abscess either in their mouth or in the throat or between two cheeks.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is within the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis in order to prevent the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it must be cut through three or four small incisions across, between the two circles, so that by the size of the incision there is no damage to the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these places can be suitable for the division of the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long outwards.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the surgeons are fearful, it is necessary that they extend the skin of the throat to the whole inch, then cut through the kneck until they reach the neck; and avoid blood vessels, if you see anything, and then sew up the incision as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe which jumps out through the broken part of the neck, and because of the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed in which one doubts strangulation, gather the two edges of the wound neatly, and all along the skin up to the cartilage; then administer medicines that create flesh until it is clean.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albacus suggests that one should not perform this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged dead, and the deficiency has been made.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	So cut off the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe properly, and they breathe through the wound instead, and in this way, you keep them from dying.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And because of this, the old man instructed to keep the wound open until the danger from the illness passes, and that danger has passed in three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they instructed to stitch up the wound and treat it until it had healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a maiden take one knife, and stab it in her throat, and cut some of the channels near the heart;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to treat her, and found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was issuing from it, and it was well that she did not have a cut vein or artery but rather the wind flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I acted quickly, and thus cleaned the wound, and treated it until it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and for the young lady there wasn't even the loss of her voice, and she returned afterwards to her usual condition;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I swear that in the surgery of the epiglottis there was no need for it.
de la grosse gorge	from the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	Thick abscesses are called "throat hernia", and they are large abscesses in the color of a raisin, and are very common among women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and follows in two ways: naturally, and accidents; or natural has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidents follow in two ways, of which one is like being full within us, and the other way is like an abscess that comes from us through the artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear, and it does not require making incisions elsewhere than in the one that is small, and the proof and search are done at every insertion:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it just like a small nut, and cannot be in any vein, then cut it, as we cut nails, and apply the treatment to every part of its casing, if there is even a little bit;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and thoroughly search for it, and treat it as appropriate until it is completely healed.
des nous	from nails
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways are there for us to do, so I will tell all the similarities.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And it is fitting that I mention all the differences that exist between us and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I state that dislocation is characterized by fever and heat persisting until the emissions have passed, and then completed decomposition; therefore, the fever and heat should subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With dislocation, there is no heat, fever or pain, and contains one gallbladder, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins also like a boil, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are based on two appearances, or greasiness, or moisture, and little change in color as I have described in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of a new injury, that you first test and inquire about all the instruments which are called 'intermediary', according to whether their shape appears or after chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the way of inquiring about abscesses is that you pinch or press the wettest part that you find inside the abscess, and turn your thumbs little by little, until you know that the instruments have reached the core, then do so according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then extract the intermediary instrument, and be careful not to rupture it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture comes to the cut, whatever its color may be, if he makes it as I have said about other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the incision no moisture comes out, knowing that it is fatty, if you make it as such about other abscesses; then cut it diagonally, and take hold of it with pincers, and lightly scrape each side of it. Carefully remove the garment where it lies under it, so that you can extract it in good health with the aid.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot extract it in one piece, then remove it bit by bit so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if there is nothing left, he returns to it repeatedly;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it stays a bit longer, and the hair doesn't bother you, apply some corrosive powder to the wound and hold the wound in place. Then put on things that soothe an abscess, heat up, and treat it with other remedies until it is clean.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the wound is large, hold the two edges of the wound together, and treat those who are having difficulty breathing due to it.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is too large or otherwise opposed and you hasten it, hold the site of the cut with vinegar powder, and let it rest for two days or three days, as long as the wound heals, then resume copper treatment that has been in use for a new wound.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the surgical instruments used for intervention, and they come in three ways: large, medium, and small; and there are four squares which are called "albaret", and one called "breb", and there are of three sizes: large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like the needles from which one removes the thorns, and they are made of citrine quartz, or iron, or silver, and yellow ones are worth more than black opals for enclosing the bends of fistulas;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And there are three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the opening in the lesion.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the hooks are like some resemblance, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if the hooks have two bends in three ways also.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And if the hooks have two bends, they are also in three ways; and if the hooks have two bends, single-hooked ones, and they are in three ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of this one that they make to be cutting, and there are some who don't cut force but from one side, of which we burn the skin, because in such cases one doesn't cut the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And these introducers are put in gloves, so that the patient does not feel it during the opening of the abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	And there are three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And none are used with much force except in the face, such as legs, arms, nipples, and around the mouth, etc.;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And no other small instrument is made, resembling pieces of bone hooks, according to this form, upon which the blood is stopped:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it should never be placed at the site of a healthy artery or veins, and under no circumstances follow this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	None of them causes the breasts to swell in some men until they seem like female breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	And they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them should do it according to this form of this line B, until 14 g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to fill the wound, then join the two edges of the wound for sewing, and continue the treatment until it heals;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the nipple is pushed downwards due to its size so it happens in women, if they cut it into two halves above, by two similar slits;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	because of which one holds onto the other at the end of each other, so that the longer line contains the smaller according to this form, until this line b up to line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and follow what we have instructed about stitches and powders, and whatever is needed for treatment until it has healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it has not healed, or if the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, it is necessary for you to fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave it until he starts eating again and remove the fat as well, then treat him until he has healed completely.
des apostemes des asselles	removal of abscesses from the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Wounds that come from abscesses are manners of hard scrophules where there are nodes, and if there are any containing moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b. until the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, you should fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and apply ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses resemble scrophules, cut them as we have said in cuts on scrophules, and if the wound is full of pus, apply a cautery as we have said previously.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sewn up, it often results in many abscesses, and similarly happens with the inflamed vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one knows this when it's due to an artery, then the abscesses are long in length.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when you feel it with your fingers, if you feel resistance; and when it's due to the vein, there's an obvious swelling.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And it's madness to remove this abscess, and indeed when it is on the breasts and armpits and around the neck and in other parts of their bodies, and they are very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	So one must avoid iron treatment, and the one on the head should also be avoided, and in the case where it is inflamed by a vein, do this above the skin for its length.

puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat with the accompanying ointment as long as it remains sound.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	And if the abscess is due to the size of the vein, it's necessary that you color with your hand whatever part of the abscess you can reach until all the pus.

et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the threads will hold, then take another needle with all two threads on every pus, at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four turns;

des apostemes des ners	The removals of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, when an abscess forms in the artery and vein, abscesses also form on nerves when they are cut, or due to excessive labor, and similar conditions.
