And if it is large, suspend it at the navel, and cut off the skin, then remove the bone, and join the wound together with stitches, and continue treatment until healed.
des grosses boces pendans	And for the larger blisters, hang them.

quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil burns
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	When the appearance comes from a wound cautery or a cut in syphilitic disease, it is on the belly and in some areas of the beard, as happens in other cuts, or blood flow that stops due to veins or arteries according to what is described, or through windiness;

Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it's a simple matter, and opens well when you press it with your hand, not constraining it; and if it's due to blood, it opens through these signs big and hard abscesses, being placed according to quantity;

And if it's due to windiness, it's soothing at the thumb, and veins so when you look at their appearance they resemble blood from the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	It is necessary to let the wound heal itself. For there is doubt and fear as I have explained in the chapter on abscesses, for both arteries and veins.

dou chancre	and gangrene
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the symptoms of gangrene and how to treat it with medicine, as well as how to avoid iron treatment. Now we will say that gangrene starts in the armpit, requiring great caution during treatment. It is said by the old ones that if gangrene appears in a place where you can scrape it off like gangrene found under breasts, on cooking areas, and other such places, it must be completely removed when it begins; but for large and old gangrene, you should not touch it because I have never seen anyone heal from it, nor has anyone healed from it before my time.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when they are in place where they can be removed as we have said, is that you purge once the black lump; then let the surgeon know if there has been a manifest swelling, and then prepare the wound. i.e., clean it up so that the operation can take place; then wash off all your onions or gangrene, and all around them without leaving anything behind; and let the bleeding go on freely, and wipe your hand well against any surface, and if the bleeding goes against the cut of the artery or vein when you cauterize, do it until the wound is healed; then proceed with other treatment until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Regarding dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have discussed the signs of dropsy in division and how this assembly of water is made, and the symptoms for each sign, and treatment given through medicines, and that done by iron: these are solely clear; it should not involve iron in these two signs: it means, pleurisy and yposarcia, because it's a mortal thing; thus when using medicines on this dropsy-like symptom called 'eclites', and if the medicine treatment doesn't help, you must observe whether the patient is weak or has another disease besides dropsy, such as stomach pain and other similar conditions; in that case, don't touch with iron because there's uncertainty; and if you see the patient's condition very greenish, and they have only dropsy without any other illness, and they're neither too young nor too old, then it would be appropriate to operate:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lift the patient's leg to your hands and have the attendants press the belly at the lowest part of the buttocks, then take the sharp lancet in this shape: And make two cuts of approximately half an inch with a pointed edge, yet do not cut too deeply so that it could reach up to the intestine when inserted, and you should not burn;

And if this is due to kidneys' issue, then do so on the right side, and it must not be that the patient lies upon the cut because the excesses should not flow towards the weaker part.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the skin with the tool and push it through, then lift your hand so that the pus-filled space between the skin and flesh is exposed as much as when scorched to the size of a fingernail or slightly more; then pierce the flesh until the pus rises halfway up, this marks the water line, then pull out the tool used for this task which looks like: And it resembles a thin silver cane, and is made of iron or brass being lightweight, and in its section there are .i. small points. On one side, .iij. points; and on another side, and .i. point; and the shoulder joint cut so that it's like a feather, this is the shape of the incision described by the author cutting the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the highest part is the gallbladder, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it starts to empty out from above the instrument; drain then half or a third of it, because if you drain more than necessary at this time, by chance the patient might die due to the release of his spirit's energy from the weapon, or he loses too much blood, or comes close to death;

fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this every day, and refrain from eating until it no longer remains but just a little water. And if you doubt about the illness, and leave much water in your body, should the wound or sand swell up, and through sweat or bath and under sunlight, and let yourself get tanned; and drink water as well; and treat with drying medicines until it becomes sane, and cauterize on the stomach and liver after the extraction of the water, just like I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Regarding the operation to correct a curved penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	No child is born without any deformities in the penis, or if there are deformities they might be small or not properly positioned. If immediate correction seems necessary and involves piercing up to one spatumile (a unit of measurement) very finely according to this shape: then place a small, thin plug of lead on it, secure it and leave it for three or four days. When the person wishes to urinate, remove the lead plug; allow urine to flow, then put it back in place; and by chance no problem occurs because the urine that comes out does not let the closure stay closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie. I have already proven this method effectively.

de la piere des femmes	From the stone of women

et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	And make the tie close to the first long tie of two spans from that one, and after these two ties leave some space which is on the left side of the knot area just before the main vein, about the span of one.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	And after all else according to the roundness that it carries; then cut in the area which is near the skin of the veins, as long as you can without cutting too deep and damaging them, just like we have explained before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Then apply wet wool in oil, and put it on the wounds, and use the bandage that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And once you have sealed with the white wax that we said, after the incision, due to concern about blood leakage.

puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then treat the wound with another remedy, until it heals perfectly.

de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from the softening of the skin of the heels
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the heels becomes soft in some people, due to the softening of the bones within, and it is something to be seen; when one wants to treat it, he must make the patient walk on his heels, and then pull out the soft skin over the natural skin; afterwards, join the two halves at one stitch, and if you can see, sew a row of stitches on top of this for 3 rows or firmly sew 4 times; then cut in between the seams, and treat it like other wounds until it heals, and remove the stitches when finished.
dou chastrement	of chastity
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Know that chastities are punished in our law, and because of this I would prefer not to speak about it in this book; and they are necessary only for two reasons: the first is for one to know how to respond when asked about them and their cure, and the second reason is that we often need chastity on certain occasions, such as with sheep and goats and cows and other animals. I thus say that chastities are done in two ways: either through attraction or through incision.
des hermofrodites	Of those who are hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions. Hermaphrodites can exist in two ways: one where between the two openings they are open like a woman's anatomy, or sometimes urinate. For their treatment and that of a man, you treat all the connected parts together, treating them as other wounds; in the second way, from men where urine jumps through the skin of the opening, there is no cure needed.
de la tentigene	Of the eczema
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Tentigene is a spot attached to the natural part, such that it's too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this needs treatment. de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Craft is first among midwives to know the figure of natural childbirth, and these signs indicate when you see the woman about to deliver internally, and smell the odor: then the child begins to forcefully emerge; thus you should understand that this birth follows its natural figure, and comes out from its head, and the placenta with it; and when you notice these signs, gently pressing her abdomen is required so the child can come forth quickly; because when descending through its head, it brings the placenta along and expels all excess fluids properly; such a birth otherwise doesn't happen naturally. Indeed, it comes from time to time on its feet, and forcefully leaves the body or the shoulders, and hands, or from her abdomen, or back, being sometimes turned by chance around her neck, and by other harmful figures; so the midwife must be wise and subtle in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures on how we should assist.

de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	From the passage of the child over his feet

de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the issue of the child on its knees

et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the infant jumps, take its feet and move them forcefully, then move its belly upwards, then I push your hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	And wait little by little; and instruct the mother to bear until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the exit of the child that comes from a wide hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to engineer to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	If one cannot bring it back, then lift the woman and walk her;

de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the birth of the child at its neck, and extends its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back.

et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	And once you've done this, make her sit on a chair of one leg, and command her to kneel; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same manner for all the second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to dealing with the second part in this way, if you're working on your second finger and there's moisture present, let that moisture drain completely;

adonques si istra legierement.	Therefore, handle it lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes they are born three or four at a time; and this is not an unusual thing, it just happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are extraordinary things, and do not live together, if we exclude them.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know this, when they are multiplied, and they are opened by the surgeon who devises them, who is bound to the fire;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And they do not come out as naturally as in all cases below, as we have said.

et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And do this so as to serve for health.
de plusors enfans	from many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	They are not married in the marris .i. or .ij. or .iij. or .iiij. or .v. or .vj. or .vij. ways, and they form themselves into child shape by the measurement of their glory. si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	If done as it should.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman who has lost her dead child or miscarried, as I've explained in the section on treatment, if it doesn't come out and you are forced to act by force.

si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if it buries the nostrils in its eyes or on its neck or in its mouth or near its palate or under the beard or on the collarbone or close to the ribs,

et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	And this is the form of the scissoring:

et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there's no remaining part, then place this rod or even higher up the body, and do this until it comes out completely.

Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom an unborn child had been bitten by death, then consulted with another on that, and treated the other's bite.

Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised, because that part of the body doesn't have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was a bone from a dead child.

dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the wife to her place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Following this comes the form of the applicator, to which the books refer; and in it are two parts for each of four limbs.

Then use your hand on all the tool, just like you have done with the pincers equally, according to the size that you see opening the mouth of the pliers, until the bone does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit. Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Don't lose hope in the tool if you haven't set it up, because its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the second stage of labor is retained during birth, it is necessary to instruct the midwife to hold her breath, and then make her exhale with contractions. And you should hold your hands on her mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if she jumps over it, it's well.

et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	And for the scab, until the fumes come within the armpit; then let it be fanned outwards, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second tooth springs up quickly.

Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if their mouth of the murrain is inflamed, we have said that there's a treatment for sneezing and herb smoke;

Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So, it is necessary then for such treatments: none of the old remedies have proved that fumigation with sowthorn and dried figs works.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used to fumigate a woman during retention of flowers and the second stage is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it appears like a reed, and one sees its hollow form, and we place the head delicately in its natural position, and the shoulders wide above the fire.
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And let there be fumigation over the coals, and the application until it is digested, and then start another one.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many infants are born who do not have their foundation pierced, but rather its site is prepared subtly with some skill.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	So it then becomes necessary in the operation that she puncture exactly where it is due, and does not pierce through any sharp tissues, and guards the incision so as to prevent contact with it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on wet wool in wine and oil, then apply the balm until it is cleansed.

And if you doubt that it will not reoccur, then put a thorn in or near the place and leave the person immobile for some days, and remove it when the child begins to walk around indoors.

And there should be no sudden setbacks from wounds or abscesses; if you encounter such setbacks, apply the same treatment as we have described for thorns.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula from its foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are nodal, and grow larger than those that come from underneath outwardly, or in the space of two parts,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is one fistula or more; and when that node is old, it works, and soon produces moisture that appears white or fine sand.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	And these are always Persian fistulas; and they are known by the person experiencing an expulsion or windiness when the patient expels something, and sometimes an odor.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if to fistulas that penetrate up to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; and extend up to the knee joint, and up to the root of the testicles.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows if the fistula penetrates to the base, and not through it:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And mark if you can feel your index finger or base against it, and insert a fine needle or spider's leg in the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has twists and turns, then you can insert a fine tent or a horse hair, as long as you feel the tent or hair on your index finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	And if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge of pus or wind, nor any smell, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	Know that she does not puncture completely; if you hasten to cure her.

Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	This wound originates near the neck and is straightforward, if there's no distinction between it and beneath the chin, but if something within the neck or artery has been cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the nerve, if there is no other means than to let the treatment proceed, and not put any restricting thing, because it harms the nerves and causes them to recede;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not place anything cold on the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuity is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but use a warm medicine instead, such as rose oil washed in soft water, and also wash the cloth used similarly in soft water,
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	And other stones of the body according to this manner, and moist treatments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, bind it tightly with bandages, then treat until it heals properly.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and filled with blood, penetrate them or deeper than that;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, then you should uncover it, and repair it, and if necessary, cauterize;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if it is cut out of the throat, or the windpipe, and the passage is kept, through which the meat goes,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	if you cut the windpipe above the throat bone, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then set the protrusion in place, and leave it for several days, then treat with drying herbs until it is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression into the bone, then remove that too.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	And if there are bone fragments, if you can remove them all thoroughly, and those that you cannot have, if you leave them until the wound heals,
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And let it be drained and bound up.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, use the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has an abscess, treat it as described in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	From the wound of a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it's from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, then observe if there's an increase in wind around the wound: you would then know that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	And if it's not deep, and the wound is still full of blood, then don't put any powder on it or bind it up straight away for fear that the blood will clot completely within.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	Let him rest in peace, and take care of the body;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I apply an attractive ointment, and fasten it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you don't have an ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient rest on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more if necessary.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no seizure, nor ill trembling of the heart, nor one-sided movements.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	And when you see the proper conditions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Therefore, cure it with various treatments, as long as it remains sound;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal and fester, then know that there is an abscess; treat it accordingly.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple or worse, or on the back, treat it according to the person who is in front of you.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it's large, with stitches; and if it's small, with powder, and if it's impregnated in the bone, and if it has cut fragments, whether to heal the wound or remove foreign bodies if they are excised.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they're not excised, let the wound fester, and facilitate the removals.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And for other wounds on other limbs, judge similarly as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	From the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The abdominal swellings are large, medium-sized, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	From a major wound, there may be an escape of the intestines, or parts of the intestines, through which foreign objects can enter;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	And the stitches are more troublesome, and there is no time like a small wound compared to a large one,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	Therefore, when returning the intestines inside, they are stitched more carefully, if they are not already being returned stitch by stitch;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	Because when they feel cold, their intestines swell up temporarily, then go back into points,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	And it's because of this that internal wounds occur, for when we move the intestine to its place where others are two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	Know that the hernia in the belly occurs in four ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The two common stitches occur at the abdominal stitch,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the other wounds' stitches are common to other injuries;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	yet they are more precise with the abdominal stitch, and I will say each one individually and clarify them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I state that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine has escaped,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	And fixing this thing is by one of two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when they are cold, warm them in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Moisten one sponge or two-thirds of a cloth with just water,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you cook in water with a bit of vinegar and cypress and spears,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and stir the intestines until their herbs are exposed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and once this has been done, let it simmer, and cook until it is released for the purpose of reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, if moisten the intestines with water or steam, whether they be cooked or not.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by this means there is admission to little things;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, they make a little incision with the instrument by which one removes the embolisms;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	the first treatment is to make the cut as wide as the wound.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we mustn't cut without significant need or reason;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and these are the tools to split it open:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut from within at the bend and not outward, and see this shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines jump out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you reset it according to its natural form in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	do so if possible, for this is the way of movement.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large and it's in the belly area,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	if necessary, heal the patient on their back.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if she is at the belly region,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then have her head and buttocks higher than the belly parts.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if there is a rupture in the abdomen at one of those two parts,
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	If you understand this, let the removed part be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And thus, one should administer what I say in large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, use what you are equipped for,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	Then have among your hands one who ministers cuts, ready to heal every wound with his hand,
et assemble les levres;	And bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common way of suturing,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and you take one needle or more, according to the width of the wound's size,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave at the beginning of the wound an inch and a half space, and I pierce with a needle where it has an inch of strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	And pierce both the leather heads with the lead balls of the siphon.
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin inside, until you make it pierced from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and join the two siphon balls together with four ties;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then sew it with a doubled thread around both parts of the needle.
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then gather together both of the wounded areas of the wound.
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave one to two inches, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then weave the thread in the same way you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and continue this according to your skill with the needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Until all the wound is contained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and that the needles are balanced, between fine and thick,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the fine needles cut all the flesh, and the too thick ones can't enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for this reason they should be of medium thickness;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	And it is not right to bury the needles too deeply within the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	for they do not allow the wound to heal properly before the stitching;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then remove the heads of the needles, so as not to irritate the patient during sleep.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I place tents or cloths over the ends of the needles for them to be held in place.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	And let them grow until the wound has healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	And this method of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because it fits a needle in one place or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch method is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and you should join together the two ends of leather and the two ends of sinew into one needle where there is a single strong thread in the middle;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these ends four together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then pull the needle through at the part where you started piercing, just like one sews a thread;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave space between each stitch as large as a small coin;
ceste costure sevent li home,	This sewing requires time,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sew a wound where there was once an opening or belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which had been made by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's width,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it goes for the intestines well two palms of great size,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and there was a wound in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I returned the intestine to him then after it had been out for twenty-one hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound healed up to fifteen days, and I treated it, and he recovered, and was well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And when they had decided he was dying, it was a wonder;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in the middle of town where none could be found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I would change the cotton bandage on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and the lancet from the outer part up until it reaches inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When it has pierced straight through to the heart in a straight line, if it hit the spinal column or ribs where you have inserted the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the inner part to the outer side.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	And when it comes to sewing this seam, do as the marten does with its fur, by sewing neatly.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And you must allow once the stitch on one side, then take it from another, until the wound is fully healed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of stitching, as Galen correctly stated,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	It is done in such a way that no one does it, by joining the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and they apply one end of the needle to the other end like this:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	Prick with a needle or pierce near the elbow, and make the puncture only on that side.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and let both shoulders move freely;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from below up to inside.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	in both shoulders as required;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then pierce both at the lower part up to this within, in four other shoulder joints that are on the opposite side of the body;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the way of sewing and it is the most common method.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galien said so, and none of them testify to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must stitch the abdomen with two needles, or where there is thread in each;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one must push an awl from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew through wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	Know that when the rupture is inside the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The stitching of such a wound in the belly is more grievous than others.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgement of the wound is as follows, just like with other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	And this is how, when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just as the art has made it escape,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if it's within the intestine, and the cost; then apply the healing powder on that area,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the art has made it escape, then apply any available ointment until the wound stops bleeding;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And stretch out the thread, and may they sew up the needle, and mend the cloth;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat the wound as usual, until it is clean.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicines, put an old cotton cloth there, right when it starts to ooze pus,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And stir it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you need no other medicine besides for many conditions when wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will cause a connection with the main parts of the body,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is necessary for you to dip it in light oil that has been heated slightly, or in scalding oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it inside the joints, and around the joints;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	And if they feel pain or gangrene in the bowels, and it happens many times.
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	If he uses black wine as enemas, and similarly if the gangrene reaches up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And pierces internally, know that when it's the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "juvenile" cannot be healed if it is injured,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	And it's because of the thickness of veins that they are, and by the subtlety of all the body, and their approach to the nature of nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if pus jumps from the wound, if it is reset behind just like an intestine, while it's still fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and turned sour or black, then you should tie the area that is black to prevent any bleeding.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries in it;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	Then attend to what's between the ligament,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and hold both shoulders up from below the wound area until beyond it to ease the extraction when the ribs are close to exit, and heal the wound.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are intact, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	If possible, one may restore it in some houses,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that one was pierced through or had a belly punctured by a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and became stenotic and developed into a fistula, causing loss of appetite and flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I performed the treatment according to my abilities, and didn't stop refining until it was properly done, and sealed his wounds.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw that they were sealed, I feared that the patient might suffer in their belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but it stayed in better condition, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And the surgeons said that when there is a small injury in the intestine, it should be bound in this way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	Take large thorns, then join the edges of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	And when the thorn has opened the mouth, place it on the two edges,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if she pushes her mouth up;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then holds the head, and this stays in place so that it cannot slip off.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	Then continue with another tremblement in this manner as before, until the wound is completely taken care of;
et cout la plaie.	and here ends the description of the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If it lodges in the intestines, and causes no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	And one can tie up the intestine with a fine thread cut from an animal's intestine,
en teil maniere:	In a similar manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	Take the head of this thread-like piece of intestine that is most dried out,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then fasten it to the end of this thread with one thread of fine linen string.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Then thread the needle with the string, sew the intestine, and set it again at the injury.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	And this method of sowing the wound is only according to the path of hope and expectation;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and broad, especially when it's in one of the intestines, if there is no embryo or nourishment, force must be used.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	from a fistula or wherever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that any wound or abscess, when it matures, is universally called a "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	And similarly when it is sealed and begins to heal.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula corresponds to the hard, whitish swelling that follows true inflammation, where no pain can be felt,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is also covered like a bird's feather;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And never clearly as a jump, and sometimes thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	And sometimes barely at all, and other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken about the classification of wounds, that every uncured wound contains no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	this is only due to eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	This means, knowing by the smallness of the blood or scar;
ou por sa malice;	or by its malevolence;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is tough flesh inside and on the lips that doesn't allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because there is too much moisture;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	The earlobes are swollen, and the material is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	the medicine is not good in its treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption proceeds like a plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or due to the property in the region that digestion is slow and health also lags behind, being driven by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	There are passages or bones where:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and treatments with medicines in this section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	So it is necessary for me to inform you about the treatment of fistulas which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in all limbs, both inside and outside;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas coming to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the stomach, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in any of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the spinal column of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the characteristic property of the main member, and manifests like that.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are done this way lead to unsanitary healing, and there is nothing except digging, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is no fistula that lasts until I have described, and you must finish with the treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you should know how to do it, if take a spider web or iron rod, if the fistula is straight, use that;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is curved, use a delicate silver thread to guide it,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	For the water flows twistily within them;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if it formed a blind passage in your hands, you could not properly seek out its end by trial and error.
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you tried to wash it out through one of the ends,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because moisture flows from one end to another, and the condition worsens;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	Then use your skill to understand whether there is bone or nerve, and if hair exists by the mouth,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	And ask the patient to clearly express any pain they feel when you press with your hand, and determine where it is felt;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	And once you have truly identified the location, whether it's far from a joint, or near to a nerve, or an artery or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in none of the places I've mentioned, if you follow as I have instructed,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And at the outer part are bones and the fluids corrupted that are within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the treatment until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula has been properly opened in the right place, you should cut as deeply as possible,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I wettest strips of material in quaking-water and put them into the fistula until they reach to its opening.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	Until the medicine has corroded away the excess that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then I place healing ointments that promote healthy growth, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it doesn't heal with this method, then apply heat cautery as we have described,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is infected by the sinus, then treat it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerves are not obstructed or interfere with primary limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove it until all traces of corruption are gone,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cleanse with things that purify flesh as long as it remains clean;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it has become dirty, wash it the same way as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	Know that you are not yet done until the end:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if it discovers and yearns as long as you are at the bottom:
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then return to its place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this is not the case, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot heal;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other option than to leave it to natural processes;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is even a small corrupted bone, and you can extract it with tongs,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if you remove it with an instrument suitable for this task,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	And if there are many bones, treat them all, do not leave any out;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and should moisture oppose this, and there is no mistake or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	so work with moisture and heat, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you can't remove them within an hour, place on the wound something that promotes gangrene,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	And let them grow until the hair is long on top of the bone,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	Then they will have their bones slightly more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	And if it is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if only let rot until the blackness becomes entirely ossified.
puis restoure la plaie;	Then heal the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the flesh that has decayed, and the bone is affected up to its surface.
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it should be to expose and cover all the way until the decay stops, and then treat it as long as it is healed over.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a case where a fistula occurred in one person's leg.
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you seek example and assistance in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was of youth around thirty years old, who experienced a pain in his leg due to an illness that originated within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	Until the matter reached the leg, and he was affected by a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but they opened it due to their madness as much as the abscess allowed.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	And they would eat very little matter, and became a fistula, and there came much pus that all groaned from body and moisture of the flesh;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	And many infections they treated for two years, and there was no wise person in the art of manual treatment,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	As long as I was called to it, and saw his leg and the remedies that were being used for its cure,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And what was eaten away by the pus from large body parts;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And they would turn red on the body of youthfulness, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I pitched a tent in one of these ditches, and then searched all the ditches,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that each was coming against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	So I hurriedly did so and dug into one of the ditches until I discovered a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	And I found it corrupted and rotted, and the corruption had reached to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was the one who appeared to me from the rotted bone, and I thought there was no other corruption, because that which I took out;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with medicines for a long time, and could not heal it;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then restarted, and exposed the bone just as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And I found the corruption continuing inside the bone, and the pus, and then I removed it, and I focused on soldering back together the joint;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not do much more than fit inside one palm of the bone, and I made it move to all its muscles,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicine; and he recovered quickly and was joined.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and there was no need to start the operation again except for due to the weakness from the illness, which could not bear it.

Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For often there was bleeding evacuation, but it became completely bloodless,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	And from the bone of its place, a hard flesh was born, and it was well arranged and had no harm or opposite effect at all in every way, neither inside nor outside.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken anywhere in the body, it should be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take hold of it, and pull on the tip of the bone which protrudes,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and instruct that it should extend upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place another string of thicker wool than the first one, and bind it around the flesh that is inside the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	extend it so that you draw the putrid flesh away from the surface,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And uncover the flesh on the side of the body where you see a hair, for the hair doesn't wound the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a coal or a board over the bone to heat up and remove the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	it should be done until one can see and feel the corruption, and again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it,

et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and let the iron touch the bone from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the connection of two joints, then cut just that part where you can reach with your tool;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if the corruption is or pierced by hand, or pierces by foot, that thing becomes very strong.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	However, you must inquire about this corrosion, how it opened;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse in all the ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not oppose you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that there are many incisal and toothed edges for cutting these bones, according to the arrangement of the bones and their appearance,

et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the manners of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you intend to use the tool you need according to what suits it.
dou feu	by fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulders dislocate either due to internal causes, or due to external factors;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated that corrosion with the remedies and they do not benefit at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	If it's necessary to cover that limb up to its end where the corrosion comes,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if it is the case that the patient escapes through this of death, or through this flaw, which is greater, from the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and if you notice these signs, it means that the limb becomes black, as though it has been burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackness, then comes this corrosion of limb to limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	And spreading throughout the entire body; if you hurry with the copper,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it's due to the impact of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and snakes, and similar,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if it's in the head near the nose, if you treat it, and do not give it room to spread up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, if you treat at the joint, so that the corrosion does not spread up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it comes to the arm, cut where you can. And if it passes the cut, that's when people die,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no need for drastic measures beyond what his strength allows;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and do exactly as the corrosion suggests or dictates: if it affects the first joint, cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it affects only part of the body, cut throughout that part.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it ascends to the leg, then it stops at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes above the knee, there is no other issue than making the patient die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	And the way to handle or secure the limb is that you hold it both above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one part of a person's muscles from under one band, and another part of the muscles from over the other band.

et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened to one man at his house:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	He had a blackness that seemed like the mark of fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	And this burn came first to his thigh bone, spreading until it consumed all the bone.

et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	And for many years after that, the burn came back to his arm bone, and it reached me,

et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	And I also doubted whether if I cut off his hand, he would die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for his strength was weak; and he completely lost hope, and returned to his land,

et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have only included this for when someone needs something else, if it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No abscess ever comes to the inner flesh, and stays so long as to cause a large gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then it bursts and perforates, and the pus jumps out, like being in vessels, so they are also like vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin above is as fine as a yard of cloth cut.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and do not reach up to the bone or to the nerve, and such diseases are called "simple".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called a "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone from inside, it's called a "fistula";
