regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look to see if his breasts are large, and the gland which is there has a foul smell.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Then administer an enema of Egyptian medicine as described here:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take saffron, oil, and litharge, equally, and cook them in one vessel on the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	And then use this according to your need, and apply it whether hot or with honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and catheterize the abdomen, and hold the rectum in place;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	leave the medicine to act for 2 hours, then remove by pressing down;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this number of times, until the belly is relieved and the urine is restored.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	And no time is fumigated with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	When this medicine is not present, and if you need ash from the vine's wood, and pour water over it,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	Then let it drain, and use it as a suppository, until you know that the intestines are well moved;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	And if the patient cannot bear this treatment, do not use Egyptian medicine or water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	If you use a enema of water and honey or if there is a bit of mercury in it;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	Or you use an enema of honey and mixed wine, where the honey has properties to cleanse and wash.

et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And then after a bit spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then I noticed that it was twisting inside the body as well, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much at how it moved from member to member in such a way, for I had never seen this disease in this manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	In every way, I wish to have what truly ought to move pain from oneself to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I did not wish it either, as I see it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that was why women have hard breasts and exposed veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this, the constriction of wind becomes apparent;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And do not appear according to this reason among those who are delicate, and have moist bodies with responsive veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see the treatment of this illness, and if the patients feel pain from it, if you find it opening as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the wound opens both above and below quickly, then continue to treat until the constraining wind force coming from that area leaves.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and apply cautery to the wound; and if you do not see it at your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	If you want to treat someone who is experiencing wind trouble, such as putrid pills, pills made from the opium poppy, and similar other remedies.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearance and the location of their impact on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of these includes arrows that have large heads, small ones, feathered ones, and those that are soldered.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those with two angles, and of those with tongues, and of those where there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	And that which urinates in no member but does so according to two ways: or in the main body it defecates,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	just as the brain, heart, liver, kidneys, lungs, intestines, bladder, and other such organs do.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	And when it urinates then in no part of these organs, and the signs of death that I will tell you later, become evident:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you must proceed with the extraction of this arrow, for death comes after it in various stages.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when you notice this bad omen and the arrow is not entirely out, if you must push it further, then treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And when the sign of the brain occurs when the arrow has retreated and pierced through the bone, and there's a fluid that jumps out which is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	Is when blindness and numbness and speech impediments occur with redness in the eyes, along with tongue inflammation and redness, and muscle twitching and confusion of mind, leading to vomiting.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps it lacks strength from the nostrils, or from the ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And there is white moisture in the wound that resembles pus, and in this also like burn of charcoal;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if you notice this sign, take care, and pull the arrow if it is still there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it hits or pierces is that it is near the left breast, and also seems as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance, if the situate also moves like hair, and in black blood, and comes coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Thus understand that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never lets out pus is when there's no foam bursting from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient's face changes color, and they sigh loudly with a cold chill.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow exits through the buttocks cover, it's deep in the back; and there is great pain and sighing; and all the limbs from the shoulders are moving.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or stomach is hit, by chance if there's any undigested flesh from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach is hit, and there's no meat passing through the intestines in the jump, then there's no hope for treatment, nor for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow hits the bladder, and urine flows out during the jump, and patients feel intense pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms and neck, throat, shoulder, elbow, forearm, back, thigh, leg, and similar limbs, are safe depending on various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is within your nerve or artery, and it isn't venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because that's how you should handle such a situation.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened in the first house where an arrow struck or pierced through the thigh up to the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and I removed it from the other side under the ear grease, causing no particular pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I extracted an arrow that fell in the grease of the eye below the paper above.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow had been returned, and one could not reach its tip towards the shaft,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was very long like an arch Turk's arrow, as thin as one light iron rod without ears; it was cleaned well and did not bring any harmful incidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And let an arrow pass from the throat to a Christian, and this arrow was Arab with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I pulled it quickly through my cheeks, being skillful as I pulled it, and the Christian remained unharmed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And take out an arrow at one blow, where it was embedded in the chest or belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after thirty days, if his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the arrow, and fastened it to a lever, and pulled hard with it, without any mishap occurring.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see an arrow fall or be driven into the back of someone, and the wound was sealed up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	And allows the arrow to remain within, not returning to its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And finds no harm in any of these natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And there was another man, who had an arrow wound in his face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And this causes such suffering of great pain; and not many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And he pulled out an arrow from the king's thigh, where it was embedded in his own buttocks,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was leaning slightly to the right side; and the arrow was fully inserted.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was summoned for treatment after it had been three days since it occurred. I found the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried very carefully to find out but did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and there was only a burn and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it might be the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on a compress dressing under his arm for fear that his armpit would swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And showed me the head of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I placed the plaster on for several days, and quickly resolved the wound, and thus the patient suffered long suffering.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	As long as he sensed the arrow within his nose; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied corrosive antiseptic medicine to the wound for several days until it was opened.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	And attempt it, and feel the tip of the arrow which was lodged at its place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then adjusted it during the opening of the wound with this medical treatment, until the head of the arrow became visibly apparent;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and ensured that the ends were deeply inserted for four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then stretched out so that I could reach with my pliers, and did this on both sides of the wound, and it could not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Therefore never stop refining and inventing ways to design tools, until I had the first one made for two days with well-made pincers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Following what its shape will come to at the end of this chapter, until I have tried it, and I shall heal the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that cartilage near the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I would then heal it, and the wound was soldered together, and the patient was entirely well.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	And I told you about the quality of extracting some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you apply your treatment to what I do not say, for books cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters compare well with just a little bit of knowledge, and on what is current and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	prove new work, and nine tools, for the removal of foreign objects that occur in this craft.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out from their places in limbs unless by two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by their entrance into the limb, or otherwise;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And the one that comes out by chance when it enters, this is the arrow entering the flesh, and it comes out once now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump now, leave it until the horse's coat is clean under, and see its outcome;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And also if it's stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, leave her like that for some days, and remove her each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then she jumps, and if it doesn't jump, pierce the skin with a small hole until the horse's flesh under is widened, and then pull her out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the skull bone, going up to one of the brain cavities,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And some of the incidents that I have mentioned directly to the patient: if not treating them straightaway, but letting them continue until their condition is even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if an arrow comes up almost to the surface, it means death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is only embedded in the bone and does not come up to the skin,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And the patient remains without any bad incident for some days if the wound is treated properly.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it's firmly stuck like this and can't come out by force, then administer internal remedies, as I've told you; then treat the area until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow has been pushed inside the body so deeply that we can't see it, then search for it thoroughly;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then guide it with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot reach it due to the tightness of the wound, or because the arrow is deep within;
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And there are no bone, nerve or vein, if it cuts so that the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	Pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears attached to the arrow for holding it.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	remove the flesh that is stuck inside at two places where you can reach.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as long as you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And handle carefully to ensure you don't break the arrowhead, but pull it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't achieve it in one go, until the arrow reaches your hand, let it get stuck there, then pull it out because the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding prevents you from proceeding as we have instructed for treatment in this chapter, then follow what we have told you about treatment.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of incising near nerves and veins, and proceed as carefully as possible to extract the arrow without risk.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	immediately or quickly, or firmly or gently; and position the patient according to their shape when the arrow hit them,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because it's the greatest help that I can provide, and if you cannot do so, place them according to what the marks show to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that came from another side, or if there is anything visible or felt swollen under the skin where it was struck:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut then upwards, as long as the pliers can grasp, and then pull: if you jump now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held within the bone, turn your hand around, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then guide it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then restart the extraction until it comes out forcefully;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is attached to the arrow, if you push it all the way down;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if it is in the cavity and you're supposed to administer force, do so with an instrument or tool,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	if the tip of the arrow enters through the skin of the tool; and then apply force,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if it is stuck in the tool, use the pointed end of the tool to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrowhead is bent, it's necessary for you to bend all the flesh around or at the point of entry, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it should be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is in or pierces or enters the abdomen or bladder or ribs and it is close by, and you can feel it beneath the skin, if one feels for it,
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and protect against cutting into the vein and nerve, then extract it, then suture the wound; that is the task.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And treat until she is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows resemble bird beaks, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium-sized, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feathers of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	by pressing at the tip of the arrow, as this is its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape for pressing and holding, as shown here, is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins through which one cures, there are thirty-one, from which sixteen have their origin.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This is to know: two small ones that are after the ears, which are called the "two herbs";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two visible temples;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins that are inside the two eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is on the head near the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugulars which are at the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are inside the cheeks above the mouth, and these veins are called "augueherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And two veins that are on the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which we usually heal are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic vein, and it's located under the left rib, and they call this 'vein of the head';
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the median one is called 'the artery', and it's made up of the cephalic vein and the basilic vein,;
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And they call this part of the body "the heart's vein"; and the great vein is situated on the right side of the body,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And they refer to it as 'the belly's vein', and it is located on the left flank.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	It refers to the one that is treated, which opens clearly on the abdomen.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	The artery is the vein that lies between the little finger and the ring finger, and it extends for two inches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and there are two veins in each leg and each foot: one is at the bend of the knee on the left side of the body,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second one at the ankle on the right side of the body; and the vein that is called "the nesse", which is located in the ankle on the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are two veins above those.[1]
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The health of the veins that occur after the ears helps with colic pains and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of a healthy person, as I tell you, and it is that you grow the hair until they are long and even; and if they start to poke at their base when they're born, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub the arm or veins with a rough cloth; then narrow the skin at the neck of the wound with a needle,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins can be seen behind the ears in the two arms depending from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Place your hand on your pulse, and where you feel the beat under your hand, mark it lord of the wound;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the scalpel, and make an incision through your vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upstream,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	And cut and remove flesh and the vein very carefully up to 2 inches deep, and let out blood as long as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then tighten and bind it until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already spoken of the incision and cautery, or in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it turns to ancient inflammation,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and for the eyes, and long accustomed earache, and within the body of the weeping fevers, they are the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the quality of the surgeon is such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is that the patient forces his neck, until the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And he feels the pulse at his throat, and then presses to feel for it;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lifts the knee above the vein on your right index finger, and holds the scalpel there;
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then lift the vein upwards, and grasp it, just as you have done in other veins, and make the cut according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, place your finger on the vein for an hour, then place it on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then make the cut, and keep it open until it heals; and we have discussed this and about its treatment and extraction, or where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The treatment of the vein from the forehead is as important as that for the temporal vein in diseases affecting the face, and it causes headache, and redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality lies in how the patient narrows their throat by twisting, causing the vein to appear.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the tool which is called "the digger", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another object, and let the blood flow according to the amount you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release the discomfort from the neck and tie the vein as long as it is healthy and has not been cut once;
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Always, it is not fitting that the flames be too close; and they are applied across, because the bone is near, and by chance break the flames when they are fine.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The treatment of the two veins that are in the two eyeballs helps with the eyes, and at the nose, and on the cheek, and in the ear for hearing, and diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of its treatment is such that when applied to patients, their disease forces its way out through twisting with some line, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then apply the treatment, and let the treatment go through in a straight line, a bit long like the flame, a bit wide, for there is no meat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps they break; then channel some blood, as much as you need to, and then bind it with cotton, binding it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The treatment of the vein near the nose is good for fever, and for sudden swelling, and for diseases of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraines and redness that comes to the face, and indeed when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of this treatment is that the patient narrows their throat, then strains their nose towards your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	Take a fine long flame, and insert it inside the mouth in the space that is between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well yet, and the arrow will now begin to move;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too far into it, and let the blood flow gently according to your need, then leave her for a night, for she is quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is how it is with the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The healing of the two intestines aids in the constriction of the small intestine, and at the beginning of mixing disorders, and in many diseases, and in dysentery, and corrosion, and herpes, and inflammations;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of healing is such that the patient's stomach compresses its lumen from both ends, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And when the masters are positioned on the head of the patient's stomach, and the stomach presses against one point,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then heal the vein along a bit more broadly than long, then drain off the blood in moderation, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then redo the operation on the other vein, then release the tie, and hold the veins moderately tight.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Let the patient not suffer from strangulation; and leave them until morning, so that the wound heals properly.
De la sainie des leivres	Regarding the care of wounds
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The care of veins in the mouth aids in their condition, and it deals with gum decay, cracks on lips, nosebleeds, and inner cheeks.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of health is to have the patient stand before you, and hold their neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at both veins, one being on the right lip and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and recognize them by their darkness, and because within they have small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then touch both of them, and if you do not know which one they are, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	If you cut off the largest portion of each part, and do exactly the same with both major veins that are above and below it, because this is one identical method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the healing near the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The healing of the veins near the tongue helps after the healing of the head (region), and this is done at the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the healer is such that when the patient lies with their hands over their head in front of the sun, and they lift the tongue, you look under each side where a black vein appears:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	So then for both, do not overdo it on either side, because near them are arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm that we commonly treat are treated in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by causing them to be pierced with one broad flame, or with a fine olive oil if the veins are like that of an ax blade, and they are called 'anisel';
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and fine according to the size and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame dart is quite famous and very wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it requires to open the veins full of large visible blood, and those contain large blood and disturbance;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more slender and pointed, and used for clarifying subtle veins, or it has subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The treatment of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are around the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is proper for the surgeon to heal carefully, and he must guard against the artery that is around.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and blood begins to flow out, it is necessary to stop the bleeding, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And it should not be held by the flame, but trimmed like that.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open clearly, it is necessary to extract it and use another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	You want no cut in it, or you make an incision in its place where the vein runs through the arm: it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and put the flame to it at once, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you know where the vein lies, it is appropriate to lift the arm in such a way that you press on the spot until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark where you will cut, and then bind the arm, and prepare to open the vein before it.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And beware not to cut into the artery when you see where it swells, because that's where the artery is: listen there instead.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it bulging up high like the urine of a child, and the veins are red and subtle, know that these are veins from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten then, place your thumb for a while, then remove your thumb when the veins are constricted, as has often happened;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	He binds the arm, and leaves it like this, not moving the patient; and remains under fear, not moving him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not cleaned, and it needs to be done, and you do not have the medicine at hand, then cut through the artery if it opens, for the head of the injured party retreats; clean the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a bark from a willow tree, and cut it, and take one half and bind it firmly until the other side.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the wound is cleaned, that's good; if not, then treat it as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the treatments are not harmed by many arrangements for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the link of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The healing of the vein in its middle is helped by means such as bleeding from above and below, and through the belly,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	Because it consists of the basilica and the cephalic [systems], just like we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And it is necessary for the surgeon to be aware of the nerve which is below, and if he doesn't go far enough, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it swells and the health is harmed, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens many times, and if it doesn't open in any places due to its subtlety, then it is necessary for you to sharpen the tool beforehand; and listen carefully as you use your power on the nerve.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there's a vein between the two nerves, cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The healing of the temporal artery helps, since it carries blood to the head, and aids with the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to heal by burning with an olive flame or with a thyme flame, for this is the safest of all veins, because there is neither loss of nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Through every way, it is necessary to seek the lightest limb and do not be discouraged if the first attempt fails, and one tries again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance inflames some limbs in certain individuals even if the first attempt fails, but there is no reason for concern.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of healing depends on your thought process.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you need to know about surgery is that it's carried out solely for the purpose of preserving health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent illnesses from occurring;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and ensure the surgery is done in one of the three veins known as head vein, arm vein and basilic vein; that is, the head vein, the arm vein, and the basilic vein.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and surgery should be performed at the beginning of prayers while kneeling, and in autumn and after meals during winter, when signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And one should nurse properly the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The care given for diseases does not have a set time, but rather depends on the need of the day or food, in all hours and at any times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not advisable to nurse children up to twelve years old, nor a woman who has been pregnant for only three-quarters of a month up until seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	And one should not nurse the elderly who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when one wishes to heal oneself, in whatever manner that may be, it is necessary for them to expel the bowels with a gentle enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If there is much of food held back, so that the veins do not draw off the superfluities from the bowels that harm the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Nor will such a person be healed who is too full of meats, or who is drunk, as long as they are able-bodied, or have dropsy;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and when one attends to healing after colic pain, and vomiting, and abdominal bloating, and frequent urination, and sexual activity, and work, of staying awake and being exposed, and that which drains away the virtue, or due to something from injury or damage to the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then regulate the body's fluids; if someone is overweight due to food and drinks or medications, then adjust their intake accordingly.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then through bathing, if there is no obstruction, for the purification of blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal it from the lower part up to three-quarters inside the belly button, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and protect yourself that day from work, from pain, and from excess, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And bind and join them, and have the bandages higher than where one is being treated, and rub the arm twice or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then loosen the tie a bit in the middle, for when it's too tight or not enough, one cannot correct it without;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the arm with your hands until the veins swell and you feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then moisten the bandages with a little old oil, then place your left hand's index finger under that vein near the arm slightly where you want to treat.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	that the blood does not escape and fail when struck by the metal.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flow like strings under the hand, and there are some that are full of wind.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	yet when one places them over the flame, they move towards the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus one is of those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for in such cases one must have knowledge of these things for the surgeons.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if they operate on the vein for the first time, that is good; and if not, then attempt it again slightly near where the limb was or above quickly, while the limb isn't swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and the patient feels pain, then they should leave it for one or two days, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	By chance, an abscess might appear; do not enter water or bathe, then start the healing if it suits her.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the wound is small or the abscess is subtle and you doubt that there isn't as much blood coming out as you see, pierce the same in this case straight through to all the flame.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And the work progresses somewhat quickly, so that the limbs are swollen; for this happens many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see that the limb is swelling, do not restart the treatment immediately, and place a little oil on it instead, for it helps lighten the body of blood, and is effective in this part where the oil is applied.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And apply the oil when you treat each wound that heals the veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And this same makes tournips and beets when you apply it to the limb; if too large for blood, its efficacy is subtle and diminishes.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, just as when the blood flow is not strong enough for that particular occasion or when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you hurry, and place on the limb a wet sponge in water and wine and a little warm, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	it is necessary that you do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if it stays on the limb for some days without turning black or green, then it does not harm him/her;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see that the wound has not healed, place on it something made from myrrh or aloes mixed with a decoction of rue, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often, pus and appearance would occur at the healing of the basilica: so then put your hand over, and if you find the body soft under the pressure of the hand, that is the sign of bad health.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hear then that you do not place upon any thing of what we have said, because it could happen in the middle without the artery; but make one plastered area dry to harden the body, then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And lead each person to have blood according to the amount of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the heart is black, let him bleed until it becomes red; and if you see that it's large, let him bleed until it thins; and if it's too hot, let him cool down.

Des sainies de ventouse	Cures using a suction cup
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blasping devices are made of horns, or spiders, or snails; and bloodletting is performed in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this kind of bloodletting which involves piercing is done in two ways: either it is by any fire, or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And bloodletting that involves piercing and the extraction of blood takes place during twelve of the body's seasons,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	One of them extends down to the throat; and the other goes up into the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And two others on each of the ribs under the neck; and the suction cup under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the suction cup on each shoulder; and the suction cup over the knuckles;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the suction cups on both arms; and the suction cups on both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the suction cup at each ankle; and the suction does not deal with blood, but only minor veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And for this reason does not weaken me at all, as we do with strength of veins;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered, nor with any fire or sense of heat, in any illness that comes from overfullness, until all the organs are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if it must be used due to the necessity of diseases or by custom, we should administer it each hour at the beginning of her period, or towards its end, and throughout, in every circumstance;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they need to bleed, have trouble with their head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And if one finds congestion and warmth within their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and in their eyes;

Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the suction cup is as follows: you should place it initially empty and apply suction consistently, then do so quickly, move evenly, and continue without stopping until you see the skin turning red and swelling. Then remove them and be careful about body positions because there are those with thick skin and clear pores: it's necessary to pierce only once, and to make wide incisions that are somewhat deep; and suction lightly.
