Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has two and a half spans wide at the bottom, and near the middle there is a small notch as to pierce an object like sticking an awl in it,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And if it is of an iron, heat it until it does not hurt the patient when placing it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And have in the middle a rod across made of an iron or a fishbone, to place a candle in charge.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And let them be both large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the suck-pipes for children are different from those for the elderly, and those for skinny people are different from those for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must place this suction cup thus on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take the wax candle or a line of one inch, and insert it through the ventouse which is placed through the penis which is also inside the ventouse.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the flame is at the bottom of the suction cup, ensuring it does not burn the skin;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and you should do so at the point we have described, so that when one wants to, steam escapes from it, and removes the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And follow the groove as before, and repeat this often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup then, which is administered in pleurisy illness, for all acute conditions, there should be no excess or deficiency, and it's only given when it's full of water, and placed solely on the limb;
et c’est li forme:	And this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Nostril plugs are only used for in limbs where one cannot place suction cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And during their unclothed state from childbirth, like two or three, and others similar;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And concerning the quality of bathing such that when you find veins in calm, clear water without contamination, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put one nut into gentle water until they are familiar and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then bleed them with a scalpel or suction cup, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place the veins on.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full, and cry out, if there is a place where we can put the suction cup, then place it, for this hardly matters after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the side with ease and water, quite well, and then proceed with the incision;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the limbs swell too much after the course of the veins, moisten with one and a half a linen cloth in cold water, and place it, until the vein becomes swollen;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if there are multiple veins, apply powdered vitriol or gallstones, and similar substances, until it becomes swollen;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Here you place half the thickness of peeled peas inside the limb, and leave them until they heat up to the limb, then it will stop bleeding now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take others without fail.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the veins do not readily take, rub with fresh bleeding, or you stick an awl in the limb until blood comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then place them, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will heat up;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see they are giving birth, if you apply a powder of aloes and ground wheat, or ash, they will now be able to push.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book on fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fracture and alleviation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear fellow, that the leaves of this chapter are filled with things not found in any of the old books, nor did anyone read a letter from them;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And because of this reason, the knowledge has been removed from our land, for I have never found anyone good;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing else, but through the study of ancient books, which I have so diligently pursued that I have dealt with this knowledge in them, and by experimentation, and through my daily routine.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described in this chapter what is contained, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the tools that are used, as I did in those two chapters previously.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	So it is necessary that we outline or introduce this book's main points and chapters where the wise people use their understanding, and remain faithful to truth. Let those who have experienced this know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when there is a break or dislocation or twisting or sprain anywhere, it should be that you quickly tend the patient on both sides and the other side, if no injury comes to them completely, such as weakness of limbs, children, or elderly people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	Or when one is too hot or too cold; and eat icy foods, meaning cold jousts, and seed of birds and fawns, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and fill your body with foods that do not completely obstruct the veins as long as you doubt about pus formation or the spreading of material in the limbs; if revive the patient to their previous state until they used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with foods that cause a heavy digestion or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and onions, and nuts, and pies, and beef stomachs, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at times, after an operation, it can move again more quickly than the breaking.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones broken in old and weak people do not heal or join well according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too soft, such as children's bones.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but take care, reset over the broken bone. that is, use large thorns to hold the limbs together until it feels as before; and do not finish his work immediately, for this requires fattening with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from the fracture of the heel, or of the leg, and in this chapter I will tell you all ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others through cutting, such as the length of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it's a fracture with injury, or a fracture with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for each kind there is its own tool and proper instrument in the repair, according to what memory brings to its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known that the breaking of the bone occurs when the leg twists, and opens well outward, and ends under pressure from the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twist nor pain at the joint, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it can well have a twist, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	But do not move it with your hand yourself, but apply the remedies that follow, and then gently constrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that when the breaking occurred in the field, and the two parts were separated, they should now put them at an equal point, so that the abscesses are placed both there and across.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if the pus is flowing out, let him not leave any day until the pus has calmed down;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then place it evenly as you can do lightly and wisely, knowing that restoring this is easier than restoring those with pieces. Then apply pressure, as described later on.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and it is divided into two parts, whether they're hands or feet, or at your hand if it's a smaller limb, or at two strings, or at one string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And position the limb according to its natural shape, so when the parts of the injured member are healed, you must set it back in all ways that allow motion within their limits as much as you can, and ensure that through your actions no injury or pain befalls the patient;
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And adjust well the two joints of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And hold it well in your hand if you feel that it is not properly set: if it is dressed beautifully, and do not over-tighten, do not press as they do when they remove an abscess by their method of incision and contraction on the limb, as we have desired many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is set properly, take care to keep the patient immobile, whether awake or asleep, whether turning over or in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And ensure that the limb is so securely set that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it is not quite right, and you should place it in such a position that it does not feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and make sure it is placed correctly, so that there is no twisting when you reset it;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the limb after breakage should be according to what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that limbs broken are varied by size and extent and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, such as hands and arms, and alike: one should wrap them in soft and delicate linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And those that are large, such as thighs and legs: it should be wrapped in a wide and firm bandage because the wide bandages encompass all of the larger limb, and restrict uniformly from all sides so there is no unevenness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then apply lightweight bandages around, three or four times according to the limb, and hold your hand slightly along the entire bandage, then move upwards from the fracture and restrict less, so the fracture moves a little away from the break;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften that bond a little bit by a little bit, until you have taken a large portion of the healthy part, then take another bond and return to it again quickly around the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then go back to the area of the breakage, and apply moderate pressure, neither too hard nor too softly, as we have said in the first instruction above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the tied linen bands until they are uniform, then tie everything with one band above, and then put your well-made stars on it, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something soothing for the abscess, and that reduces swelling, and leaves it like that for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then grasp them firmly, and make them half the size of a medium stick cut straight, or from wood used to create darts, or from palm fronds, and shape them as in this illustration:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the splint placed on the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and should also be as long as it is appropriate to the size of the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold them in place just like you did with the first splinting process, then tie an extra piece of string on top of that, as you did at the first splinting around the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	As the wound is larger before, now it's smaller; it requires that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the thread is thick, like what I want from works of fools who make their loops on linen cords twisted in the wrong way, and this is great error, because the loop cannot be even if it's too delicate, and it doesn't suit to have less than half a do (a unit of length) between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are irritated by the edges of the stitches after tightening during their healing, then place linen patches or raveled wool on them, so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is inflamed and the ribs are broken, I will then describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not proper to hold back too much of your efforts when healing broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when limbs are large, it is not proper to apply too much force in the first few days or even up to seven days, or longer according to your assessment of each new development.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method of the old plastering practice to restore fractures, dislocations and twists: you take flour that remains in the mill's walls, mix it with plenty of egg, and create a paste that isn't too thin or too thick. Use this concoction as needed; this is the common way to use plaster to restore fractures in various positions, even for women and children, because neither excessive heat nor coldness should be applied.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering to restore fractures and dislocations: take three parts of each of these: barley meal, dandelion, rue, and asafetida, along with gum arabic and myrrh; measure it out to be .x. three times the amount specified for each individual ingredient. Mix in a bit of myrrh and aloes also at .v. five times. Add seven parts of alechil (a type of vinegar). Grind all ingredients into powder, then mix with plenty of egg. If the mixture is warm to touch, use this plaster; it has good composition properties and rapidly heals broken bones and is beneficial for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method for dressing in the case of twisting: take mugwort and myrrh, each in 3 parts; frankincense and aloes, each in 8 parts; castor oil in 6 parts; Armenian balm in 10 parts. Grind well and mix with vinegar or abundant egg yolk, then administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method for dressing wounds and fractures in bones that are displaced from their positions, to alleviate the pain associated with them, and for bone injuries: take new wool, and cook it in lard and oil, then apply it onto the wound. These bandages do not heal immediately, but they are better for soothing abscesses and properly relieving bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method for dressing broken bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial plantain leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method for plastering during the restoration of bone fracture and removing pus. Take root of vismaltive, camomile, flowers of violet, meal of yarrow, one part from each; grind them together, mix with wine, and when the limb is warmed, mix it with coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another way of applying plaster more effectively than the first one, when pus is returning during member's restoration. Take roots of vismaltive and linseed, balm, melilot, and saxifrage, as well as violet and camomile flowers from all these gather a part; grind them together, mix with salty water or sweet water or wine according to the heat of the limb and its rest period.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates instructs that only beeswax ointment made of wax and oil should be applied to the broken limb for restoration without anything else. He states that it must not be too soft or too hard but just right.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that we should place upon the broken limb for restoration, substances slightly heated and somewhat dry, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to prepare plaster for injury and pain: take mung beans and chicken feathers from cooked chickens, or bird feathers, and basil leaves, and sand equally ground, grind them, make the mixture into plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then after a little while, be sure that the patient does not feel any pain and that there is no movement of the bone in its place; if you do not relieve the pain with your hands.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the limb, or itching, if you feel no rest or swelling, hurry and relieve it, and apply the plaster now; take a lightweight cloth and a wet sea sponge, dip them in water, then immerse the limb until the itching stops and the pain is relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then allow the limb to rest for an hour, then place it on dry wool, soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it with a cloth until you are sure of removing any pus.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation settle in the limb, and alleviate the pain, then resume gentle movement, and a bit of plaster, but do not bind it as tightly as before; and proceed with subtlety until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you notice that pus is coming out and the area is red, painful, swollen and oozing, indicating inflammation throughout, then you will need to apply plaster and bind it, start again as you did initially, in exactly the same way.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have said happens to the limb, and it does not respond by releasing anything as described, or if you need to loosen it only after three days, four days, five days, or seven; and each time let it rest for twenty days, according to what can be seen, until the swelling subsides, and brings closer alignment of the bone.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then you must hold the restriction longer than before, and the animal will fatten its flesh as I have said previously; and if you notice that the skin is drying more than necessary, understand that no remedies can come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then regularly apply hot water to it each time you reset the joint, and do this once every third day, and drain a little of the fluid.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this procedure then cut out the pus from the limb, and hasten healing as the ignorant do, who forcibly straighten the bent limb: that is wrong, and it produces poor outcomes; I see no other remedy than to let nature take its course and heal properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Regarding various methods of breaking bones
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of fractures exist, and various shapes, and their causes are specific;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the collarbone breaks right up to the syfac which is below the bone, just like in an arrow wound or cudgel hit; thus it is called this type of fracture "arrow-wound" or "cudgel-wound".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing it, this is called "absolute" fracture; and these are either large or small wounds resulting from such fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or crack, or fracture of the stone collarbone, or under the stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture partly through, which approaches until it reaches the membrane beneath the bone, or above the bone, and this wound may be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that penetrates into the bone as thin as a hair, and this fracture is small, and because of this it's called this "hairline" fracture;
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made or caused by striking with a stone or falling, or by something similar, and causes part of the bone to break inside out, and makes the joints uneven just like when goldsmiths melt down pots; if the metal enters inside the pot when they are melting them.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more in those with wet bones below their head, such as children's bones;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And happens through all these methods of breaking up that small fragments are removed as with bones; and I will discuss them in their proper place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And know all methods of breaking through the diminution upon them, and the examination by touch, and through the corrupt flesh that is upon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known by this: when one has exposed the bone and rubs inside it, if the breakage shows black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a breakage, beware of any bad accidents due to illness, if you see no harmful incident, such as vomiting bile, loss of intellect, extension and rigidity, fever ague, and if the eyes emerge and turn red, or show other similar symptoms in various conditions, you cannot be certain of recovery.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a terrible accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the nose comes to you first, and it is in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the month.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in winter, you should hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day after the month; so that when the pus around the bone becomes infected, and accidents as we said occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone breaks up to the membrane covering the brain, then you should split the broken part like this: take hold of the piece from the diseased flesh and uncover it on the bone in all possible ways, and more according to the shape of the wound as much as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if the flow of blood comes to uncover the bone, or an abscess cavity appears, you should use what is necessary, and it is that you fill the area with wet linen saturated in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And let the wound rest until the abscess cavity subsides and blood flow resumes; then begin inside the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two surgical methods: one of these methods involves making a narrow incision upfront, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut that is larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have several different size cuts, some narrow and others wide, all pointed and made of iron; and execute them lightly, so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is protruding and hard, it's necessary for you to pierce through internally, so that you make cuts with needles, not fully piercing until beyond the bone surface, and there should be a margin or about half a circle above the point, ensuring the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have more than one, so that each goes into its place of the bone's thickness, so that you have needles for all parts; and this is the form of the three types of needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce through the broken bone is that you place one needle on the bone and turn with your hands until you know that the bone has been pierced. Then put the needle in another spot a bit after, and do this for all around, then cut out the space of the bone which is between the teeth, doing it more finely than you can and gently as we said, as long as you bring the bone to your hand or any tool you have such as forceps; and make sure not to touch the brain nor the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and removed the bone, it is necessary that you prepare what remains of the bone from one to another similar tool but it should be more precise and finer than the other incisor;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if it remains none of the small bones, nor any scales, treat them lightly with surgical instruments; then heal the wound using the methods and remedies we have spoken about.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of doing this is as Galien taught, which is more safe; and it uses strong tools, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, it is necessary to uncover a part of the bone, at the place where the fracture opens and moves, so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place under the tip of this lens-shaped incision, from which its shape is given:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side only, and make the cut at half a rib, so that when you are cutting, it is against the bone; then strike with a small hammer upwards, so that you gently crush the entire bone, and take care not to damage the cloth that is underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it's close to the bone, gently squeeze the bone, for the bone responds well without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture doesn't penetrate just to the membrane, and the bone is cut only from above, with small pieces present, then after that abrasiveness, and remove the scales with a subtle razor you must have in various quantities, for administering the most suitable one to each area according to the treatise and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you are in front of large razors, and after even finer ones, and never cease doing this until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other scalp cuttings and finer fractures, it is necessary that you apply treatment according to their orientation; and this matter is not answered by someone who has put their study into this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is discovered by him, it is necessary that you take one linen bandage according to the size of the wound, and smear it with oil from roses, and place it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another double bandage and smear it with wine and oil from roses, and place it on the first bandage; and do this more gently than you can so as not to weigh down the wound, then apply a second layer of linen and don't pull it too tightly just until it touches the wound only;
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And leave it like this for one or two days until the abscesses ease off, then remove it and apply remedies such as lily roots, corn flour, incense powder, and arisole, and similar things; prepare a powder from these and apply it to the wound, and after that administer medicated ointments without irritation;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And ensure that the wound is clean immediately after it occurs, do not leave pus behind and avoid having bandages stick together. For when bandages stick to the brain tissue, they can spread and cause great harm. Because when something sharp is placed over it, it invades from above causing injury to the patient.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Then be careful therefore, if no accidents come to the patient as we have said, there is doubt without fear.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if fear only comes from the medicine that we have placed there, and should it have this virtue, then you must take a portion of honey, and three parts of rose oil and mix them with one spoonful of vinegar, and apply it to the affected area;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then follow the methods of treatment as needed, until there is no bleeding.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that never are broken the two parts below the nose or only one of them, because they are two bones; and this one below is cartilaginous, it does not break, even if you bend or twist it, then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you bend your little finger or at the nose, and place this break evenly inside your second finger, and through to the knuckle forward, until the nose regains its natural shape according to its form;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain through your operation.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose and cannot come to the nostrils, it must be that you put it level with the tip of a hair a bit thick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, remake another, and try to restore the first on the same day if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	But if not, after the seventh or eighth day when the abscess has calmed down, then apply to the tip of the nose with bandages of linen, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you apply another one from the other side, if the break is in that direction; and make them large enough to fill the hollows of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they say that one should moisten the tents with butter and change them each day. I do not think this is correct, but it seems better to moisten them in the preparation of an egg broth, and powdered cornmeal; then leave the tent until the bone becomes hard, and the cartilage toughens.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes, one should use goose feathers instead of tents, and if you have an egg, wrap it in them, and keep the warmth, allowing the air to circulate among the wounds; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pus comes out through the nose as you work on it, then apply a wet cloth or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a little pot of almond oil.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscesses are not treated, one should apply a poultice externally, made from ground herbs and incense powder mixed with beaten egg yolks. Then place it on light dressings and do not bind them too tightly;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the bones are broken into small pieces and have been fractured into many parts, one should use suitable tools for this task. Then open the wound, clean it from fragments of bone, stitch or glue it together, as appropriate bandages or salves suitable for this kind of injury would be;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound within the bone, then treat the wound, and apply garlic, until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured and there is no wound on the surface, and only the breakage is external, not at all broken into two halves but rather split internally throughout, one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture occurs in the right part, to place your index finger in the mouth on the side of the injury; and if the fracture occurs in the left mandible, you should place your index finger of your right hand on the injured side, and gently apply pressure to the fracture internally, then press it outward with the other hand from outside, ensuring it is even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is divided into two parts, then it is necessary to provide extension for both halves, ensuring they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth start moving or break, or you have to stitch them back together using a thread of gold, silver or silk. Then place wax on the broken jaw and put two layers of linen on it. Place under one layer a large ridge made well or a piece of leather matching in length and width according to the jaw size. Secure this at the ends that you can reach and instruct the patient to rest, and let them consume light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, release it on the third day and then put things back in order according to what has changed; apply plaster, mixed with powdered materials or enough eggs or flour of chestnut, after removing the wax. Place a light woolen cloth over the plaster, and if the plaster dries and the patient's position remains unchanged, let them rest until they heal. Many times healing occurs within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And when pus comes out during an incision, then apply what we have instructed many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward nothing of the bone that has been removed; so much delicacy was required in using tools suitable for this task.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there remains nothing, if the wound is wide, place one plaster suitable for it over it to promote healing until it heals.
de la forcele	By the power of
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks many times before reaching the shoulder, and the breaking occurs in three ways: sometimes it is broken and torn into two parts, resulting in fragments that are easier to restore; or there's tearing with an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedures are as follows when there's tearing with an injury: you need two assistants, so that one marks the shoulder where the force is broken; and the other extends their arm towards the affected part. Then make the break equal with your hands, ensuring the shape matches what it should be, without any sign of strain or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round sponge of cloth or wool under the shoulder to the hair, and make its size according to your need; then stretch and lift up the force, hold the sponge in your hand so that you can make the break equal as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the force outwards due to it coming forward, so that the patient lies on their back, and places a half pillow under their shoulder, and pushes the shoulder blade downwards, until the bone of the force is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then apply pressure with your fingers, and if you find fragments, it is necessary to cut through them; and gently pull the pieces apart. If the bone cannot join at any point from pressure, make a cut near one of your incisions; but place this tool on the force, in order to prevent leakage:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And shape it like a spoon, do not place it inside, and make it as wide as you deem fit, according to the size of the bone and the strength of your operation; and have two holes, as you see, and let one be broad, and the other narrow, just as is the wound you made when treating the bones:
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are certain of the removal of pus, if you should clean the wound, and if its rupture is small, or if there's doubt about the removal of pus, then dress the wound with bandages and tents, according to their quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if pus comes out, if moisture arrives, apply oil roses and vinegar and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The grinding of bone, when it is sensitive to wounds and sensitive to the tailor's work, is that you place on the bone a plaster made from powder from the mill and yolk of egg, and put light cloths on top, and place an apple under the armpit if needed;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very large band about the size of a palm wide, then put two layers of cloth on top of the cloths and plaster; then take a slender pole one and a half spans long and wide, wrap it around that band, making sure the end of the band hangs down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And place the torch on the wound, and turn the bend towards the neck, and over the healthy elbow, and over the diseased elbow; and reset from each part, and when you see that the joint keeps the wound attached, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then reward each day, and when you release the bandage, then restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	And let the disease heal on its back, and put him when he sleeps, a small pillow under the elbow, to lift the shoulder up; this will ease the strain of the wound from the force by aligning the shoulder blade, or you tie his arm around the neck, and do not remove it unless bad accidents occur, for up to twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then restart the plastering if you see that he needs it, and tighten and leave him like this until he recovers; and she is recovered at most in twenty-six days, and less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Sometimes the shoulder breaks or splits from its joint, either at the top or in the middle, and not by force; when it is hit where the break has occurred. Treat according to the shape of the fracture, and reset as per its natural form, in all ways that you can. Then apply with ground powder from a mill, along with plenty of egg whites, lightly tucking them in, and place two layers of cloth above. After this, place a large, thin board, somewhat wider than the shoulder, beneath the fracture area; ensure there is no movement at any point on the shoulder when placing the board, and use strips of linen to secure it evenly so that the board stays firmly in place without moving from its position. Keep checking each day; whenever it begins to heal, tighten again, adjust the board if it has moved out of place, and keep the patient lying on their side with the injured shoulder. The shoulder will be healed after 20 days or possibly 25, If this number of days is completed, then remove the dislocation, you can be sure; it isn't simply bone that is able to settle easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone piece appears first and not below the knee, then proceed by removing it, along with the abscess beneath, and do as we have instructed for treating wounds of muscle dislocation.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it breaks often at the end. And when it is broken through, it leans downwards, causing great pain to the patient and lack of mobility immediately, and suddenly, and by chance vomits blood, and opens inside the broken bone, and one feels this very well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it comes to setting the bone, should lie lay under his backbones, and you place one span between the shoulders, then press on the shoulders, and join the ribs of both sides with your hands, and gradually adjust them evenly in all possible ways until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place plaster bandages over this fine structure of salt or another lightweight substance, wrap them in a piece of cloth, and tie them around the broken bone so that they do not move. Then bend the joint back onto the back, press against it properly, and reward every hour by massaging the wound area; if she begins to heal, then tighten her up; and if it is appropriate to remove, due to corrosion or itchiness coming from the body, or pain or abscess, act quickly, and loosen the tie, and remove the plaster bandage, and treat the person who came in with the cure methods. Then replace the bandage, and press it until it is fit for use.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs happens only in the large ones after the back and within, and do not bend because they are oily; and one feels it well during examination at the waist.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And for the repair, if it is to equalize the breakage, just like it should. And then apply the plaster, and press with a thimble, if you need to.

And if the breaking of the ribs is occurring internally, the patient feels great pain and piercing, like from labor pains, because the bone punctures the tissue; and they have pains all over, immediately and vomit much blood, and it's a serious health issue, and the elderly have experienced severe illness.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer meats which swell the belly, in order to expel the wind from outside.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not follow this, for abscesses and pus do not come about unless they have arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have arrived, heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And it is said by none of us to apply suckling pigs over the wound in order to extract moisture and this appears reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the suction cup draws away excesses from the body due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine. Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels intense pain that cannot be borne by the bone piercing the skin, there is doubt for the patient as to whether they should cut through the wound of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place one or two instruments under the cloth; then you must slice the bone and drain lightly, and afterwards stitch the two edges of the wound if it's large, and treat with plasters until it heals. And when abscesses occur, place moist cloths in a rose oil and place them over the wound; and treat as needed for the abscesses, being vigilant where necessary on the rib or where it should be, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the break at the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No fracture occurs at the bones of the neck, and it does not bend; similarly for the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure. Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this incident does not happen to him, then it is a simpler thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you should extract if there is pus, if it's placed on the spine or on the yolk of an egg, until it calms down; then place on one of the soothing plasters and let them dry, and bind with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where they feel pain, until they recover.

And if any bone is broken, then it should be covered with plaster; and remove the bone, then join the two edges of the wound, if they're large, with stitches, then treat with ointment that heals flesh until it's healed; and if the tip of the bone is broken off, which is called 'the tip of the elbow', then you should hold your left hand pouch and place it evenly on the other to your power, then apply the plaster and bandage as needed; then press firmly, and if there are broken bones, then remove them and treat the wound until it's healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	From the breaking of the bone of the hip

It occurs when the bone of the hip is broken. de la brisure de l’ajutoire	From the breaking of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The assistants are those that lie between the handle and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of these two methods: wherein one method involves taking a full length staff of medium thickness, in this manner:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two shoulder blades with two strips each, and place them on top, securing the patient's sides onto one spot. Then, lay the broken arm onto the staff until it reaches to the middle, making a bend of the staff halfway through, then rest it against any heavy object or let assistants hold it downwards; then place the broken end of the shoulder in alignment with his hands when they are together, up until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you place the patient on their back, and tie their hand to their neck, then instruct two assistants to have one cut off from where it's broken in his hands, and the other cuts off everything up to one finger length, stretching each one to its respective side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.
