And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, hold a bandage right over the wound and above it, spreading each minister to their part. And if the wound is close to the head of the shoulder, it should be that you place half a bandage under the elbow, and another towards the knife, below the wound; and also if the wound is in front of the knife, it should be that you put a light bandage, without effort, as long as the wound is equal up to the middle, and up to the knife; then make the cut even as it should be, and hold tight, so no pus comes out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if pus comes out from it even after seven days, do not hold tightly any more; instead apply greased wool and oil roset, until the pus coming out is calmed down. Then hold tight, so when you place the plaster on the wound, then unite the arm with the shoulder support, put your hand on the shoulder or chest; apply the bandage and hold it tight both on the support and on the arm, ensuring that the arm stays straight, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you suspect that the bone does not move, use supports for this, and place a larger and stronger support under each cut than the others, leaving an inch of space between each support. Ensure that each support is large enough to pass through the wound three inches from both sides; then hold tightly on the supports as I instructed at the beginning of this chapter concerning wounds, more firmly but not stretching too far apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the base of the nails, and the constriction, as we have said, in your care when returning a broken limb, and you doubt about removing an abscess, should it be left to bind for up to seven days, as we have said; then check each day over the next three days the binding, making sure there is no itching or swelling that appears on the site, or that the infection cannot reach the body because it is too tight. If this happens, if we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such events occur, or if the limb is not released until after two days or more, and remains warm on its back, with his hands on his stomach; place under the shoulder one thick cloth of wool evenly, and observe every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the bandage becomes soft; if it heals by the power of medicine, and give him the meat we have placed before, in such a way that the meat is at first tender; and when he begins to recover, then it should be large. And it's customary for the shoulder and leg to be recovered within forty days from all; and thereafter you must release and administer baths and medicines of ointments for the body to heal. If there are uneven folds or constriction, then it must remain for dislocation up to three days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the 'fosciles', from which one is small, and it's this that covers the pit; and the other is large, and it's this that rests under, near the small bone; by chance only the large foscile breaks or the small one, or by chance they both break.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small fosciles are broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; and when the large ones are broken, the healing goes wrong, causing more distress than when they were broken together. If it's only the small foscile that breaks, then gently stretching a bit is what's needed, and setting them even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large foscile that breaks, then you need to apply more pressure; and extend on one cushion, and place the pit of your hand higher than the others, and have the smaller bones lower than the other bones, and ensure they are crooked towards themselves, and another cushion in front of them a bit higher, so that the bones do not suffer any strain. Then stretch out your assistant's arm to the part below their hand, or at one inch, and have another attendant on the other side above. And then place the mirrors evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break into pieces, you place each one in its own location, and if there is none that grabs onto the bone, and you cannot restore it to its location, then do it upon and through the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is an injury due to the breakage, I spoke about it in the singular chapter; take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if during the commencement of the restoration there occur abscesses, apply glue; that is, a strip of tallow made from rosin and white beeswax, such that it is neither too hard nor too soft. Then place one strip by delicately spreading it upwards until the abscesses are relieved. Afterward remove the tallow and spread with abundance egg powder on the powder mill, then place the sticks, making sure that each stick of the breakage is directly beneath it and somewhat more outward than the others; and know that there should be seven or eight sticks in various arrangements: whether the breakage is within one bone, two bones; and hold more above the breakage than elsewhere, as we have said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the bandages covering the breakage be moist and soft, but not hard nor abrasive; and may the thread, from which these are woven, be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin. And rest the limb and the ligament for a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad occurrences come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you immerse the limb in hot water until that itch subsides; and let the limb not be allowed to rest. And then resume the constriction, and once the bandage is removed and the bone has been revealed, and assuming there's a similar situation, guide it back into place.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if precautions are taken so that no further constriction can come to the limb because it's too tight, it is necessary to soften it with heat and let it rest for a few days until the constriction ceases, then resume constriction.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things we have discussed come to pass in the patient, or if it takes up to twenty days for them, then they can move their hands near their neck, and ensure that their necks are level, while being careful about movement and digestion, sleeping on their back; and know that this strain will be restored in thirty days or forty days, and by chance within twenty days, depending on the compositions and the qualities of the patient.
de la brisure de la main	of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that in the back of the hand and on us, few breaks occur, and only fold many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the heel of the hand is broken or folds, it should be treated by having the patient sit upright and directly in front of themself; then place their hand flat on the table and stretch out the fingers of the broken parts, and align the bones properly, making sure they are well connected; and apply bandages and splints, if no abscesses develop, then place an ointment according to the size of the injury; and wrap it in one linen sheet.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is at the base of the fingers near the belly of the hand sole, make a pyramid from cloths and instruct the patient to hold it against their broken finger; then stretch him with a long cloth, and place the splint as high as the size of the hand's palm, making sure it stretches properly.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the front, it must be that you place one splint above and another below on the foot part. So that your hands are open and straight; then tie them entirely around the hand, and seal the joint between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of the two feet, it's like a bundle, just as should be; and press with the heel, and if you see fit to place a small upright splint to raise the fracture, and not move. And if the break is at the other foot, like in the index or one of others, it's like a bundle, and tie with the healthy one which comes after; or you tie all together, as long as they can hold, or place an upright splint just like for dressing; and take care in restoring and arranging each wound separately, and adapt to what comes up, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the shoulder often breaks several times, and one can see it when it turns in front and behind; and its repair is this: i.e., the first step being to set the broken part above the breakage point, and the second below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the veins lie on its surface, then extend each minister's line to its equal part; and this is when the breakage occurs inside the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the breakage is close to the root of the shoulder, then have one line towards the elbow and the other lines over the breakage. And similarly if it's near the hip joint, so put the lines behind the hip joint, and the extension downwards; then place the bones at an equal distance from their two ends, as long as they follow its natural shape, and then apply plaster, and bind it, since abscesses do not come about there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is pus to remove, let it heal first before you return to your work and treatment; the wound is made in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the burn .i. bandage twice or three times, and retain the excess, then bend the leg until the heels reach the base of the calf, and place one long thread between the shin and the leg, down to the knee, and guide the ends of the thread over the top; then bend around the leg and around the shin with the bandage, then place a splint on the burn, and place a splint on the bone of the leg; then insert your hand in between the leg and shin with cloth for equal pressure, then begin to bind firmly .iij. times or four times around the burn; and as you go beyond the burn, bind less tightly; then take two threads that you have placed between the leg and shin, and bind them three times above each other, then return down below the thread until you are underfoot; and tighten, so that it does not move from its place, then leave him like this, until no pus, swelling or similar sign appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, release it and address what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that catch hold, it should be removed, so long as one can; and if one cannot, it is necessary to cut the wound and draw out the strength; and treat him as we have said, until he heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no part of the flesh is broken when these pins are inserted in such places, as in the shoulder and on the arm; nevertheless, no inconvenience affects the patient in this manner of restoration.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the flesh is restored within one day, or somewhat less, or somewhat more, depending on the variety of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the groove of the knee there is little breaking, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it's mostly just a crack, or missing a bit of bone (about an inch), and this happens to all wounds, whether open or closed, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to place it even with what was round at its ends until it's assembled and moves as it should. Then put on plaster, and add a round stick if needed, then tighten appropriately. Afterwards adjust every arrangement that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as pus formation or similar conditions; for each situation apply what suits it until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Regarding the breaking of the leg.
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	You know that there are two bones in the leg, from which one is called by its right name "ham" and the other is called "foscile"; and any kind of injury or breakage happens just as it does with the arm, and for this reason the restoration process is exactly the same as for the arm, and the procedures are all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, then twist the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then twist in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the larger bones are broken, one feels great pain and can see clearly; then twist in the air. Then apply extension, making it level, and tie the ligaments equally; but still, when the breakage is ugly, and there are many fragments, the extension should be less intense and gentler; and adjust according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two lengths of wadded cloth that cover the leg on both sides and are long enough from the thigh down to below. Then wrap these around with two pieces of bandage above and below, and tie them in the middle as well; so that the leg does not bend either to the right or left, and thus is done properly; and no one should administer to it a single piece of cloth as long as the leg, made of wood, and place this under the leg to prevent movement. This should be carried out exactly where there is damage from the breakage or wound; and move the leg each day in order to check for pus or any other complication; treat it until it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From the breaking of bones at the knee
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle it does not come from breaking, but when bones at the knee are broken, there is a break and in the legs, powerlessness occurs in multiple positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the bones at the knee break, and you see these bones thrusting over one another, place these limbs of earth under your feet just as if they were going somewhere, then put now your foot on his, where the bones are elevated, press them so much until their heels revive; then set plaster and bindings over it, and put a small table at two feet thick under the belly of the knee, then restrain him to the foot insertion, then when you have wrapped cloths around him, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, remove the bandage, for you will find that the bones are equal, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the ribs are broken, repair them, as we have said about the ribs of the hand; then place a splint on the broken rib according to its length, and make it slightly wider than that. Then put under the splint the board I mentioned, and apply pressure evenly; and if there are two or three or more broken ribs, break them, placing one splint for each rib according to its size, wrapped in a single linen cloth of the first, then fix the board under the patient's abdomen where it is cut. And while lying on the table top above the patient's belly, ensure that it properly cuts through.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other matters I have discussed regarding other injuries, once we have talked about them; and correct each incident according to how it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Regarding the breaking of the bone in the hand.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of natural pregnancy is broken, if it gets enlarged, then let her stay on her side and incline her to the part at the back, held from behind. Then fill the gap that nature has provided with cotton, also put in as much as one thumb's width. Next, release the woman, lift up her back little by little, then, let the cotton jump out until it comes to the opening of nature and the bone returns with the fetus; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, put it back in again, do this for seven days or more. The break will be restored. If you see fit, take a goatskin bladder, tie on the nozzle end a stick, fill the bladder entirely within nature; then blow forcefully through the stick until the bladder inflates inside: nature will return to restore the break. Then fill it with cotton and leave it like this for several days or until healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the wrist in an animal is broken, or in a woman, if it is restored in such a manner as we have said for the thigh bone; and these broken bones are not to be overlooked by those who put their study and use into them, and read my book. For the breaking indicates more than various positions the right path of restoration: therefore, understand this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of a broken penis, take an oxtail and fill it with the penis; then wrap it tightly in bandages, and let it be for three days or longer, and it will heal very quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	By fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it's large, like in the case of the thigh bone or shoulder blade or similar, that they be surgically treated now, so that the surgeries we have mentioned testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, then seal it with vitriol, or if you have nothing else, then start to treat the fracture at that same hour, or on that day, assuming no abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses appear, then let the treatment continue until a new day, as long as the abscess is calming down, and don't touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause harmful accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken and visible at its exposed knee, then it should be put back together lightly with your hands, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not available to make it even with your hands, then you use this tool made of iron, which is seven inches or six inches long, and its width matches the size of the wound; for this task, the surgeon must adjust its size as needed for each treatment of a broken bone; it should be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend under compression on your limb during surgery, and it should be sharp in front, and large at the middle towards the front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche" because the curved bones should be placed on the visible part of the bone; and strike once, until it heals, and ensure they are even against each other. And if the breakage is subtle, and the tools cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must hold the top of the bone as long as the tool can manage this task.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone back, as we have said, if you have an appropriate tool for this task, such as a scalpel or awl, with your skill; then take out what is remaining in the hard and small cuts of the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is returned, and if the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it's not in its natural position. Do as much as possible to get it into its natural position, then moisten with one or two drops of black vinegar ointment, provided this is appropriate; and similarly, if it is suitable for healing; do not place bandages or any other substance on the wound if there is an infection; avoid causing infection and decay at the wound site. Once you have restored the bone, apply these treatments accordingly, let the wound remain open, cover everything properly based on the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound isn't constrained with breakage; and many times such actions result in the patient experiencing illness or corrosion; and make sure to use softer and less intense compresses compared to other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is deep or large and you suspect that there might be complications, as we have said, and if you find pain in the area, it's not suitable to apply treatments; but envelop everything inside instead of applying them, using hard bandages and securing them. And when after one or two days or three days you see blood coming out of the wound, remove what you have placed with all wine, and apply healing ointment for wounds, such as the tetrafarmaçon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it must be that you dislocate the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is joined and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it should have been so that the limb is bound in such a way that the bone slides down slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it continues for the whole day, and it cannot join anymore, know that there are small fragments of bone, so you must seek to open the wound with a probe, and remove all these necessary pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula comes to the bone, or any other way of corruption, you must treat it according to what he said in his chapter above. And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the bone of the heel or shoulder blade, and other similar bones of large limbs, do not try to remove them, for many times death comes from this, but leave it until it heals; perhaps it will heal after twenty days or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The burns that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They come many times after the wound has healed, especially near joints, and an ugly thing to see is the appearance of the limb; and by chance it cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if there is any swelling: if you administer restorative medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, as well as sanguine collyrium, caraway, and similar others, do so with one of these things, or all together, and mix them with stinging wine, or with a whole egg or with honey; then apply this mixture on the spot in poultices, bind it tightly, and don't release it by hand for several days; then remove it, and repeat another application until the swellings are gone. Or you can apply this on a well-made piece of leather because the properties of leather have the ability to drain all swellings from the limbs; if the swelling has turned hard like stone and needs to be removed, if there is any excess, make it obvious; or continue applying it until it's reduced by any barber, until it's gone, and continue treatment until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the limb that becomes weak after an illness.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone has been restored, and after that the limbs are weak and subtle, this happens due to certain reasons: because one is for those who were bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many ligaments, and could not allow the necessary movements in the limb; or for an excess of bleeding; or for overly large movements, not at their proper time; or because they lack much blood within their body, being feeble.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you must make the patient eat the medicine, and make the body tender until the pus multiplies within him; then give him baths, and bring him joy and ease. After this, apply grease to the limb, so that the grease attracts to the large pus, and washes it often with hot water until the pus aligns with the limb; and restores its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The member becomes twisted after recovery.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and if the bones break open, even though the body's natural form is lost, it does not lose its function: nor should one believe those who say that we must break all new members completely; many fools do this in our land. These practices are criticized and cause great harms, sometimes leading to death. However, when the fractures and injuries are fresh, they should be immersed in hot water or cooked with soothing herbs like dandelion leaves, roots, and milk thistle, among others. And one should apply a poultice made from these soothing substances; you take greasy figs, grind them with cinnamon, and similar medicines that alleviate heat. Then you make a greased plaster and apply it. Or you take greasy dates and grind them with nutmeg powder, and other such medicinal substances to cool down the heat. And then you make a greased poultice and apply it.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And never should bone be rubbed continuously and for a long time with wet hands. And have the limb moved every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twists have aged and hardened, like bones, and require being treated with iron, if it is necessary to cover up to the bone, apply subtle gentle cutting at the incision; and include consideration and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the patient.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation affects none, if now is needed bring back without hesitation.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the joints swell up, and by chance, when they are placed back into their position; because it is not proper to move them at the moment they are swollen: many times, they bring on pus and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	If this happens, have a surgeon attend the patient, then let him stay until all abscesses are relieved; then immerse the limb in warm water and oil, then gently realign it, treating each limb as its treatment would be appropriate for its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have organized the chapters about shoulder dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jaws become dislocated backward, and the dislocations of both are according to two ways: or they are slightly bone-like from their places, and somewhat softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the heels, and causing saliva from the mouth that one cannot hold, nor can close his mouth, and wraps his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can often return through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accomplished, you should reset it quickly without delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the ministers cut near the patient's mouth, and insert one of their fingers into the base of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth; if the dislocation is two inches (ij. pars) then the other hand should extend outside to match; instruct the patient to soften, his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And guide her until she settles back into its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it becomes difficult to return them, even when the two jaws are together, if they were raised with hot water and oil, until you gently reset them; do not overly strain during the resetting process, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned evenly, and the mouth of the patient is closed tightly after soothing it, place wet cloths as bandages in a poultice made of rose oil and beeswax, then bind them gently with moist linens.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient rest on their back, and if they are dislocated, have them lying between two cushions, so that they don't move to either side or force themselves to twist, but please feed them light food until the pains subside, and secure the jaws.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then let him chew lightly, and do not make any effort to open the mouth for eating or drinking until the mandible is well set and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be properly aligned within an hour and are not converted back to their original positions, then fevers and recurrent swelling occur, along with occasional abdominal discomfort, and occasionally, vomiting of pure fluids.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it's a loss; and many times, death occurs to the one who experiences this within seven days.
de la forcelle	from the lever
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The strength cannot relieve from within the middle of the back and at its base, and is dislocated outwards every time, and one feels this well indeed.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the process consists in laying the patient on their back and stretching their arms out; then press down firmly onto the affected area with your palm and it will return. Then place them on a plaster bed and use the bolster, pressing it down tightly;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the shoulder which is close to the blade cannot be reset; if it isn't and if it becomes dislocated once, then you should reset it at its original position as we have said. Then place them on a plaster bed with the bolster, press tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until they are sane.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And similarly, the shoulder blades of the back are brought back when it is removed from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Concerning the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one way is when it dislocates from the part of the scapula to behind; and the second is at the part near the elbow; and by chance it dislocates above, which happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And the shoulder does not dislocate behind or within the nerves; and it dislocates from below towards the scapula more often, especially in those who have little flesh, because with them it happens quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps to bones, and returns to bones.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, some men suffer from impact or fracture, and the shoulder swells due to an abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must test them until you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And you will recognize dislocations when it is moved towards the shoulder blade, and makes a distinction between the diseased and the healthy shoulder, and you will find a clear manifestation of their diversity among them;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and from the shoulder blade to the elbow, as if it were an arm. And the patient cannot bring their hand back to their nose, nor move it with any movements;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And also, if it is dislocated at the top, even though it may not be completely hidden, because you clearly find it at the elbow;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this way of dislocation can only be remedied when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts his hand from the malady at the top, then places his fingers on the shoulder blade, and raises the joint to its full extent at the top above him; and the minister lifts his hand and extends it up high, putting it under; if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and the minister must apply soothing and calming remedies, such as decoctions of thyme and fenugreek and clover in water, and they should be applied.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then cover the back of the patient with a strip of cloth, and place on the shoulder blade a poultice of an even consistency, neither too soft nor too hard, then place a stone under it. Put the heel of your foot on the stone, lift the head of the shoulder gently, and pull the hand towards the malady.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another minister cuts the neck of the patient, so that it doesn't move forward; this shoulder returns now and then, and if you notice it being reset in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And make sure the person is present in a larger space than necessary for the patient; and stands straight towards the side, and pushes the shoulder against the ribcage, and lifts the ribcage up slightly so that the patient hangs down in an upright position;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another minister pulls the hand of the patient towards the belly. And if the patient is too light, you can place something heavy with them and then pull their shoulder down; the dislocation will return now and again.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And another way to reset is: take a long stick and bury it in the ground so that your shoulder is also at about the level of one pistol, and not too large or too small;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then have the patient placed on their side, but with their arm held up, and the arm should remain as long as the length of the stick. Then extend their hand down from the other side to form a shape, and the joint will return to its place quickly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return through all these things that we have said, do this treatment: take one and a half arms of thick oak wood and four large sticks, which should allow the head to be inserted from below evenly up to the shoulder, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then bind the head to the stick with a piece of cloth underneath, so that the stick does not bruise the patient's arm, then place the stick under the arm against the side; and extend your hand up along the stick from the elbow, and fix the shoulder on the stick, and the arm at the elbow joint, then place your arm on one of the stakes about the width of a thumb, and keep the other hand hanging down, leaving the body hanging from the opposite side: the joint will return to its place now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when she is there, in whatever way it may be, if you must put on the seat of the dislocation an equal thread, then place plastered with powder from the mill, together with incense and egg oil, all over the shoulder and around it. Then remove that which was placed upon the seat after a while, and retie the bandage on top of the plastering, and hold the hand at its neck, and keep your hands in this state for some time.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is required that he chew a little, until the limbs are strengthened, for it will heal faster; and then continue to chew more after five or seven days, and move it around; and if it's firm and not softened, it will have healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is loose due to moisture that has caused it or for another reason, it is necessary to apply three applications of heat (cauterization), as was explained in the section on cauterizations before or chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it gets dislocated after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift your arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is torn or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint would never be properly placed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation near the buttocks, and breasts, or behind, if it is caused by pushing and stretching of hands, or administered elsewhere; treat until it's healed sanely.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there comes weakness in the limb, and delayed movements, then the patient should take frequent baths with hot water until that weakness is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	From the dislocation of the shoulder joint
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the shoulder joint is dislocated at points and returns to them; and if it's dislocated from all sides, even in front and behind, then the shoulder dislocation doesn't respond properly, as you can see it clearly and feel it well; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you connect the shoulder bone with healthy tissue, you can see it clearly. For the joint is rough and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder to any extent.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	It is necessary that you reset it in this manner as abscesses heal from within outward, for if they heal from outside inward, it would be problematic to reposition them; and by chance, they may not be able to be fully returned; shoulder dislocation is worse than others, and causes more intense pain, and by chance death occurs.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is as follows: when it can be brought back to that position where one can extend their hands to your two hands; and their arms are spread out, and the hands face each other in line with the elbow joint, both inside and outside, then push the joint towards their wrists or at the base of their palm until they return to their place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if there is a dislocation in front, it returns when they double their hand against their own and push from the base of the palm with the knife that has been inserted.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it doesn't want to return to its place, then apply strong extension; and let each administer extend their arm, and hold them both together, so that they don't move during the extension. Then rotate the arm from each side, then when you have wrapped a long and wide cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when the joints are joined by your hand, if you apply some oil to soften the joint, then press on the joint firmly until it recovers;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it's in place, apply dry plaster with an egg yolk on top, hold it firmly in place, and allow the arm to be bent at the neck by the shoulder, leaving it for a few days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, remove the bandage and leave it as it is; and if you see that the joint does not heal well, reapply the plaster and the bandage, and keep it like this for a few more days until it's firmly set; then remove it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if it feels sore after the removal of the joint, and it moves again, wash and scrub beautifully, pressing until it is relieved; or you can put a layer of fatty lamb's wool on the joint, then leave it for one day and night, then reapply and let it enter into a bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when it sweats, rub the joint gently, then set it back in place, and then immerse it or bathe with water; and do this two times or three times until it heals; and if you see fit, apply moistened cow fat mixed with butter to it, and apply it; if it returns to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand joint has dislocated, and the return is slight, more so than other joints. In this case, it's necessary to quickly bring it back into place while it's still dislocated, thus making sure that the limbs swell or an abscess arises.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the resetting is such that you place your hand on a board and extend the minister's hand, then you make them equal so their palm touches the appearance of the joint, and press until it reattaches.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	In all cases, you must check if it is in its proper place; then have the patient lie down on their back with their hand extended and moved to determine the placement.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, have the patient place their hand's back on the table, and you position your hand over that appearance of the joint. If it returns to its proper place now, then it is correctly done.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If that doesn't work, use plaster to soothe the abscesses and leave it like that without needing to restart.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you can't put it back in its place after several days, if the joint stays twisted;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And it does no harm to the patient for as long as his hands are swollen, and he cannot strain anything completely: then you will know that a nerve is cut, or an artery; if there's no other way than to apply heat with a cautery in such cases, and by chance there's no other solution.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when his hands are in place, apply the plaster we have mentioned, then strain it and leave it for five days, then release it and leave it as such.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he can't move it well and there's no crack, then apply hot water, and rub until it is clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Regarding the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	None of the fingers of the hand are dislocated separately from each other, neither on the back of the palm nor on the belly;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	So all the fingers are together, and you prevent the dislocation from occurring in your pockets until they recover, then support the head of each finger, and bend it towards the part where it is disjointed;
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	And leave it for two days, and then put them equal on the third day; and not let it move, as we have said, and release him that day, and make it move, and bind him again later; and do this often, until it is tight.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do the same if it is dislocated in the belly of the hand and do it like you did before until it becomes sound; and do the same when it is dislocated on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the heel, of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the heel, or the back, or multiple heels are dislocated, if there is no treatment, because death rushes to the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that discharges jump against their will, they cannot hold them back, and many times parts of the body soften, or both feet, or both arms, or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times, the shin bone shortens to four parts; that part which shortens at the back is called 'tuberous':
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The treatment for this is that you should reward the person if the tuberous condition came from childhood: if there is no remedy or healing at all.
